# Two-Creature Weapons Teams
Some weapons are so massive they require two creatures to move and operate them effectively. These weapons may be oversized firearms, large incendiary devices, or unwieldy melee weapons such as large drills. Though they come in many forms, they have a few common traits: they require two creatures to operate, they can be moved without hindrance by two creatures, and they must be loaded with some form of fuel and ammunition on a regular basis to be fired.

## Two-Creature Weapon Rules
Two-creature weapons require at least two creatures to operate them, and they come with the following additional rules considerations:


### The Weapons Team
The two creatures operating a two-creature weapon are known as the weapons team. The weapons team consists of a leader and a follower. Only one creature can be assigned to each role, and they cannot switch roles once assigned, even if one of the roles becomes vacant, unless they leave the weapons team and rejoin.

#### Joining a Weapons Team

Joining a two-creature weapons team costs a creature's action and half of its movement as it equips its part of the weapon. If one creature is already part of the weapons team, it may use its reaction to make an opportunity attack against the creature joining the team. Leaving a weapon team requires no action as the creature drops its part of the weapon.

A creature must have both hands available to be on a weapons team and can't pick anything else up without dropping its part of the weapon.

The creatures within a weapons team must stay within 5 feet of each other and the weapon at all times. If one of them is ever more than 5 feet away from the weapon or the other team member, it is no longer part of the team. 

#### Moving Two-Creature Weapons
The follower can no longer move on its turn except to leave the weapons team. The leader's speed becomes equal to the lowest speed among the creatures on the weapons team. Whenever the leader moves, it can choose to move the follower along with it if the follower is willing, even when the leader is moved against its will. 

#### Stealth
While part of a weapons team, a creature has disadvantage on Dexterity (Stealth) checks. Additionally, activating a two-creature weapon reveals the weapons team's location if they are hidden.



### Repairing Weapons
If a weapon has taken damage but still has at least 1 hit point, a creature can spend 1 hour or more attempting to repair the damage. The creature must have the necessary tools and parts for the repairs. After 1 hour of repair work, the creature makes an Intelligence check, adding its proficiency bonus to the check if it is proficient with the required tools. If the check succeeds, the weapon regains 2d4 + the creature's Intelligence modifier + the creature's proficiency bonus hit points. If the check fails, the weapon does not regain any hit points, but the repair can be attempted again using the same tools and replacement parts.

<img src='https://i.ibb.co/pRGXM8s/orchish-cannonade.png' style='position:absolute; top:-35px; right:0px; width:817px;' />

<img src='https://www.gmbinder.com/images/WGybwnz.png' style='position:absolute; top:90px; right:103px; width:950px; filter:  grayscale(00%) brightness(97%); transform:rotate(10deg)' />


<img src='https://www.gmbinder.com/images/WGybwnz.png' style='position:absolute; top:115px; right:-10px; width:900px; filter:  grayscale(00%) brightness(97%); transform:rotate(0deg)' />


\pagebreakNum

## Two-Creature <br> Weapon Attributes
In addition to the common attributes of size, weight, AC, HP, and damage immunity, these weapons have the following additional attributes and considerations:

### Hit Points 
A weapon has hit points that can be restored through repairs. When its hit points reach 0, the weapon becomes inoperative and irreparably damaged.

### Weapon DC 
The weapon's DC is used whenever a creature makes a check to fix mishaps, when a creature is repairing the weapon, or the weapon forces a creature to make a saving throw.

### Challenge Rating
When players face enemies equipped with fully functioning two-creature weapons, the encounter's challenge rating (CR) should be calculated as if the weapon is an additional creature with its own CR.

### Ammo / Fuel
Weapons may require ammunition, such as bullets, or fuel, such as flammable chemicals, to make attacks. This part of the stat block includes the cost of the ammo and the number of charges it has, which represents the number of times the weapon can be used before it needs to be reloaded.

### Functions
By default, weapons can have three different functions, which can each be activated as an action by creatures on their weapons teams. The Load and Crank functions <br> can be activated by the follower, and the Fire <br> function can be activated by the leader. Each <br> function can only be activated once per round. 

#### Load
This function is used by the follower to reload <br> the weapon's ammunition up to its full capacity. <br> It requires the follower to have immediate <br> access to the weapon's ammunition, and <br> creatures can use their reaction to make <br> opportunity attacks against it. If a creature hits <br> the follower this way, it drops the ammo and <br> wastes its action.

#### Crank
Not all weapons have this function. If a weapon <br> does, it must be activated by the follower before <br> each use of the Fire function to move the ammo <br> or fuel through the weapon.

#### Fire
The function is activated by the leader to fire the <br> weapon. When this function is activated, but before <br> its effect occurs, roll to see if a Mishap occurs.

\columnbreak



 If a Mishap occurs, its effects happen before the effects of the Fire. This function can't be used if the weapon is out of ammo or if the weapon has a Crank function that hasn't been used since the weapon was last loaded or fired.

### Mishaps
Mishaps represent the weapon experiencing a significant malfunction. There is always a risk of this when firing the weapon, and some weapons have other circumstances that risk a mishap. Whenever this risk occurs, roll a d6. On a result of 1, a Mishap occurs, and the creature who triggered it must roll on the weapon's Mishap Table to determine the nature of this malfunction (see the Mishap Table section).

If the weapon has less than half its hit points, roll 2d6 and take the lowest result when checking for a mishap. 

Unless stated otherwise, you must always check for a mishap when activating the Fire function.

### Passive Traits
This section describes any traits of the weapon has that don't require actions to utilize.

### Mishaps table
Most weapons have a Mishaps Table, which describes different ways their functionality can go awry under adverse conditions. When certain abilities or conditions dictate, roll on this Mishap Table.

A creature can attempt to resolve a mishap by using its action to make an ability check based on the nature of the mishap. The creature making the check can be any member of the weapons team or anyone else within reach of the weapon. If the creature is proficient with the tools required for repairs and has them at hand, it adds its proficiency bonus to the check. A successful check ends the mishap. Mishaps that do not have a Repair Check Type cannot be repaired.

<img src='https://i.ibb.co/j6sJzVB/holy-frazzle-cannon-MOM-238-mom-238-art.jpg' style='position:absolute; bottom:-0px; right:-45px; width:600px;' />

 <img src='https://www.gmbinder.com/images/cPPYV7h.png' 
  style='position:absolute;right:115px;top:-70px;height:1400px;width:1416px;transform:rotate(270deg)' />

 <img src='https://www.gmbinder.com/images/cPPYV7h.png' 
  style='position:absolute;right:115px;top:-70px;height:1400px;width:1416px;transform:rotate(290deg)' />

## Ratfolk Two-Creature Weapons
Though two-creature weapons teams are deployed by many races with the technological know-how to craft such weapons, ratfolk are among the most prolific users of such weaponry. This may be due to the combination of their technical capabilities, their willingness to take on the risks such weapons pose, and the seemingly never-ending amount of weapons designs their mad engineers concoct. Though these weapons can be hazardous to their users, ratfolk are never shy about accepting such risks if it means getting the opportunity to obliterate foes with overwhelming firepower. 

The ever-opportunistic ratfolk often mass-produce their most popular designs and sell their inventions to the highest bidder. They will often make more potent versions of these weapons as well. These masterwork variations gain sinister nicknames as their dreaded reputation builds, and they are reserved for use by the most prestigious clients of the ratfolk engineers.


### Toxic Wind Mortars
This fiendish artillery piece is an amalgamation of primitive engineering and unholy alchemy, a stark representation of the Ratfolk's cunning adaptability. Crudely crafted from rusting iron and scavenged metals, its appearance belies the terror it inflicts. It's not merely the brutish launch mechanism of a traditional mortar that warrants fear, but the horrific payload it delivers.

At the heart of this weapon lies the toxic wind - a deadly concoction of the most lethal substances the Ratfolk have extracted from their underworld environment, or synthesized through their arcane and toxic alchemy. Sealed within fragile orbs of glass, this gas waits with malevolent potential for release.

When the toxic wind mortar fires, these spheres arc high through the air, shattering on impact and spreading their malignant payload: a green, ethereal miasma that sickens, corrodes, and eventually kills those who inhale it. Armor tarnishes and rots, flesh sears and boils, and the very life-force is choked out of those caught within the cloud. The sight of this deathly fog approaching not only brings physical destruction but also instills terror, often breaking the morale of the enemy before the cloud even reaches them.

\columnbreak

___
> ## Toxic Wind Mortar
> *medium two-creature weapon (85 lb.)*
> ___
> - **Armor Class** 15 
> - **Hit Points**  60
>___
> - **Weapon DC** 15
> - **Damage Immunities** poison, psychic
> - **Challenge** 3 (700 XP)
> - **Ammo** Mortar Globe (1 round, 50g).
> ___
>
> ***Mortar Globe*** This weapon fires glass mortar globes filled with poison gas. When a mortar globe shatters, it releases a 15-foot radius sphere of poisonous gas from the point of impact, heavily obscuring the area. This cloud persists for one round or until it is dispersed by a moderate or greater wind (at least 10 miles per hour). 
>
> When a creature enters the gas cloud-covered area for the first time on its turn or begins its turn in one or more of these clouds, it must succeed on a DC 15 Constitution saving throw. On a failure, the creature takes 13 (3d8) poison damage and becomes poisoned until the end of its next turn. On a successful save, it takes half as much damage and isn't poisoned.
>
> ### Functions
>
> ***Load. (Follower Action).*** The toxic wind mortar is loaded with a Mortar Globe. If the follower drops the globe while trying to load it this way, the globe shatters at the follower's location.
>
> ***Fire (Leader Action).*** The leader targets a point within 300 feet of it that it can see and launches a Mortor Globe at that location. Each creature within 5 feet of that point is showered in broken glass from the globe and must make a DC 15 Dexterity saving throw, taking 10 (5d4) piercing damage on a failed save, or half as much damage on a successful one. The mortar globe shatters at the point

> ***Death Mortar Globe*** This weapon fires glass death mortar globes filled with poison gas. When a death mortar globe shatters, it releases a 15-foot radius sphere of poisonous gas from the point of impact, heavily obscuring the area. This cloud persists for one round or until it is dispersed by a moderate or greater wind (at least 10 miles per hour).

#### Toxic Wind Mortar Upgrades

You can apply any of the following upgrades to a toxic wind mortar. Doing so increases its CR by 1 per upgrade applied.

**Acid Blast.** When the weapon's ammo shatter at a point, each creature within 15 feet of the point must make the Dexterity saving throw against the weapon's save DC. A creature takes 7 (3d4) acid damage on a failed save and half as much damage on a successful one. (The orb still releases its gas cloud as usual.)

**Rot-Spice.** The clouds created by the weapon's ammo deal necrotic damage when shattered instead of poison damage, and creatures poisoned by the gases gain a level of exhaustion.

**Hex Razors.** When a creature moves into or within the cloud created by the weapon's ammo, it takes 5 (2d4) slashing damage for every 5 feet it travels.

#### Toxic Wind Mortar Tactics
Toxic wind mortars function as artillery and excel in providing area denial and obscuring the enemies' vision. This tactic proves highly effective when ratfolk forces need to reposition, surprise their enemies, blind opposing ranged attackers, or force them to move. Due to the delicate nature of their ammunition, Toxic wind mortar teams will use their Scurry Away feature to quickly escape whenever an enemy approaches melee range. 

The upgrades for toxic wind mortars don't alter their tactics but instead enhance their effectiveness in their existing roles.

\columnbreak

### Ratlinn Guns
A paradoxical fusion of crude engineering and subtle brilliance, the ratlinn gun is a testament to the ratfolk's knack for invention. Built from scavenged metals, timeworn wood, and the odd mysterious alloys they mine from the depths, this rapid-fire weapon is a sight to behold. It is composed of multiple rotating barrels, each capable of spitting out a hail of deadly ammunition at a terrifying rate.

The ammunition is unique to the ratfolk, handcrafted in the underbelly of their world. A mixture of sharp metal shards, stolen and scavenged munitions, and occasional nuggets of strange underworld minerals, all are melted down and recast into thousands of wicked, serrated projectiles.

<br>

___
> ## Ratlinn Gun
> *medium two-creature weapon (90 lb.)*
> ___
> - **Armor Class** 14 
> - **Hit Points**  40
>___
> - **Weapon DC** 15
> - **Damage Immunities** poison, psychic,
> - **Challenge** 3 (5,900 XP)
> - **Ammo** Hex Ammo Belt (18 rounds, 200g)
> ___
>
> ### Functions
>
> ***Load (Follower Action).*** The ratlinn gun is loaded with a Hex Ammo Belt.
>
> ***Crank (Follower Action).*** The ratlinn gun if cranked so it can be fired.
>
> ***Fire (Leader Action).*** The leader picks a target within a 200 feet to fire at. The team leader has the option to immediately fire the weapon again using the same action. This action can be repeated up to 6 times, with each shot consuming additional ammunition. The action ceases if there is no remaining ammo. 
<br>For each shot fired, the team leader must roll to determine if a mishap occurs. For each shot fired after the first one, the leader must roll a d6 for each shot fired this turn when checking for a mishap (2d6 for the second shot, 3d6 for the third, etc.) If a mishap occurs for any given shot is fired, that mishap must be resolved before more shots can be taken.
<br> The chosen target must make a DC 15 Dexterity saving throw for each time it has been targeted. For each failed save, the target suffers 13 (2d12) piercing damage and an additional 7 (2d6) radiant damage.

\columnbreak

<br><br>

When activated, the ratlinn gun roars to life, its barrels spinning in a lethal whirl. In seconds, it can transform a tranquil landscape into a storm of flying metal, shredding through ranks of foes like a scythe through wheat. The very sight and sound of the ratlinn gun is enough to break the morale of many a foe, a rapid, deafening symbol of the ratfolk's ferocity.


Yet, the ratlinn gun is not without its flaws. It is a volatile and unpredictable weapon. Overheating is common, leading to disastrous explosions that harm friend and foe alike. The ammunition, while plentiful, is inconsistent, causing unpredictable trajectories and often requiring a significant volume of fire to be effective.



___

This action can be repeated up to 6 times, with each shot consuming additional ammunition. The action ceases if there is no remaining ammo. 
<br>For each shot fired, the team leader must roll to determine if a mishap occurs. For each shot fired after the first one, the leader must roll a d6 for each shot fired this turn when checking for a mishap (2d6 for the second shot, 3d6 for the third, etc.) If a mishap occurs for any given shot is fired, that mishap must be resolved before more shots can be taken.

\pagebreakNum

##### Ratlinn Gun Mishap Table
| d6  |    Mishap Name               | Mishap Effect             |   Repair Check Type           |
|:----:|:---------------------:| :-------------------------:| :-----------------:|
| 1    | Rapid Misfires| The weapon has a critical failure, does not fire, and each creature within 10 feet of it must succeed on a Dexterity saving throw or take 26 (4d12) piercing damage plus 14 (4d6) radiant damage as stray bullets fire everywhere.| none
| 2-3 &emsp;&emsp;    | Dulled Fire | Creatures that fail their saving throws against the weapon's Fire function take only half damage. | Str
| 4-5    | Stalled Gearing | The weapon does not fire and can no longer fire more than one shot per turn. |Str
| 6    | Jam | The weapon does not fire, and its functions can't be used until this mishap ends. | Str

#### Ratlinn Gun Upgrades

You can apply any of the following upgrades to a ratlinn gun. Doing so increases its CR by 1 per upgrade applied.

**Ratlinn Coolant.** When rolling to check for a mishap with the weapon, you can choose to disregard one of the d6s you roll (if you're only rolling 1d6, you can negate the need to roll.) If the weapon incurs damage that reduces its hit points to half or less, or if a mishap occurs, the coolant bursts. The burst coolant forces each creature within a 10-foot radius of the weapon to make a DC 15 Constitution saving throw, suffering 22 (5d8) cold damage on a failed save and half as much on a successful one. The coolant burst is resolved prior to any Mishaps that triggered this event. Once the coolant bursts, the weapon loses this ability until it fully regains its hit points.

**Hemorrhaging Shots.** Whenever a creature fails a saving throw against the weapon's Fire function, it sustains a wound. At the end of each of the wounded creature's turns, it takes 2 (1d4) necrotic damage per wound. A creature can have multiple wounds simultaneously. Wounds can be healed if the creature regains 10 or more hit points, or if a use of a healer's kit is expended on it. Alternatively, the wounded creature or another creature within 5 feet can make a Wisdom (Medicine) check check against the weapon's DC as an action, ending all wounds on a success.

**On-Board Ammo Assembler.** When the follower is using the weapon's Load function, they can choose to salvage parts from an unmanned two-creature weapon or vehicle with a CR of 3 or higher within 5 feet, provided it has at least 30 hit points. Doing so inflicts 30 damage to the salvaged weapon or vehicle. If this reduces the target to 0 hit points, it is dismantled and cannot be used for further salvaging. The follower gains a special ammo belt made from the salvaged parts that lasts for one minute. While using this ammo, the weapon deals an additional 13 (2d12) damage with its Fire function, but the function triggers a Mishap on a roll of 1 or 2 when using this ammo.

\columnbreak

#### Ratlinn Gun Tactics
The ratlinn gun represents the epitome of risk-reward weaponry, with its potential to eliminate virtually any target, be it swarms of enemies or a single formidable creature. Its primary targets are foes with heavy armor and low dexterity.

As long as the fight is progressing favorably, weapons teams typically start by firing two rounds per turn. However, when victory is within grasp or defeat is imminent, the rate of fire escalates. In extreme panic or power-driven frenzy, teams fire as many rounds as possible.

##### Ratlinn Gun Upgrade Tactics
&emsp;**Ratlinn Coolant.** This safety upgrade gives weapons teams the confidence to fire three shots per turn instead of the usual two, as long as the coolant is active.

**Hemorrhaging Shots.** With this upgrade, the team is more likely to distribute their shots across multiple targets to inflict bleeding. If there's a creature effectively healing the wounds, they will focus their fire on that target, often risking more rounds per turn to eliminate it.

**On-Board Ammo Assembler.** Encounters involving multiple ratlinn guns with this upgrade can be interesting. The guns are encouraged to be more reckless, firing more shots per turn. If one of the guns experiences a malfunction, the team abandons it, and the remaining ratlinn gun teams cannibalize its parts. The increased mishap rate from the newly acquired scrap bullets means they can deliver devastating damage but with higher misfire risks. When the weapons misfire and become disabled, they contribute more scrap for the remaining ratlinn guns.

### Hexfire Throwers

Constructed from rusted metal, corroded pipes, and bizarrely vibrant crystals mined from the deep earth, the hexfire thrower is as terrifying as it is crude. It is a deceptively simple device, consisting of a large, cumbersome tank filled with a mysterious, volatile substance, connected to a projecting nozzle manipulated by its ratfolk wielder.

This enigmatic liquid, known only as "hexfire", is a product of the ratfolk's arcane knowledge and alchemical prowess. Glowing with an eerie, otherworldly light, it is said to be the physical manifestation of raw, chaotic energy harnessed and condensed. When unleashed, the hexfire clings to anything it touches, searing and consuming it with unnatural, green flames.

When the hexfire thrower is fired, a torrent of this deadly hexfire is expelled, engulfing everything in its path. The very air seems to hex and ripple around it, and the heat it generates is so intense it can melt through steel and stone alike. The sight of this horrifying green firestorm is often enough to break the will of even the most hardened warriors.

However, the hexfire thrower is a perilous weapon, even to its handlers. The hexfire is highly volatile and unpredictable, and any misstep, any fault in the device, can result in catastrophic backlashes. It's not uncommon for the thrower to explode in a ball of hexfire, consuming the ratfolk operator and those unfortunate enough to be nearby.


___

>
> ***Fire (Leader Action).*** The weapon lets a loses a torrent of fire in a 20-foot cone pointing in the direction the leader is facing. If the safety protocol has been overridden, it is a 40-foot cone instead. Each creature in the cone must make a DC 15 Dexterity saving throw, taking 18 (4d8) fire damage on a failed save, or half as much damage on a successful one.

\pagebreakNum

#### Hexfire Thrower Upgrades

You can apply any of the following upgrades to a hexfire thrower. Doing so increases its CR by 1 per upgrade applied.

**Self-Destruct Mechanism.** The team follower may use their bonus action to activate the weapon's self-destruction sequence. At the end of that creature's next turn, the weapon is destroyed in an explosion, and every creature within 30 feet of it is subjected to the weapon's Fire function.

**Motorized Pumps.** Each time the hexfire thrower is cranked, it gains a level of heat that lasts until the weapon goes one full round without being cranked. If the safety protocol is overridden, the hexfire thrower gains two levels of heat. The hexfire thrower's Fire function deals an additional 4 (1d8) fire damage for each level of heat, and when checking for a mishap, a mishap occurs if the number rolled on a d6 is equal to or less than the current heat level.

**Hex Napalm.** If a creature or a flammable object fails a saving throw against the weapon's Fire function, it ignites. Until an action is taken to douse the fire, the target suffers 9 (2d8) fire damage at the end of each of its turns.

\columnbreak

#### Hexfire Thrower Tactics
Hexfire throwers are designed to target the largest clustered group of enemies during a battle, but they always maintain a safe distance of at least 5 feet from any opponents. The weapons team will override its safety protocol whenever doing so allows them to hit two or more additional enemies. This strategy is also employed in moments of panic or when the team feels they have the upper hand.

##### Hexfire Thrower Upgrade Tactics
&emsp;**Self-Destruct Mechanism.** This upgrade perfectly aligns with ratfolk tactics. Whenever the situation becomes even slightly precarious, the team will activate the self-destruct mechanism and immediately abandon their post to avoid the ensuing explosion.

**Motorized Pumps.**  As the heat builds up and becomes unstoppable, the weapon becomes incredibly dangerous. Consequently, the ratfolk operating this weapon tend to be more reckless than other teams.

**Hex Napalm.** his weapon is best suited for a hit-and-run strategy. Ratfolk are more likely to utilize their Scurry Away feature with this weapon, forcing creatures that have failed their saving throws to decide between extinguishing the flames or using their Dash actions to chase after the weapons team. The team should prioritize setting as many creatures ablaze as possible rather than focusing on one particular group.

### Hex Grinders
Fashioned from an eerie blend of scavenged metals, ancient stone, and uncanny, glowing crystals found only in the deepest crevices of the underworld, the hex grinder stands as a testament to the ratfolk's dark intellect. It consists of a pair of interlocked, spiral-shaped drills, powered by the raw, volatile energy housed within the strange crystals.

These drills, when activated, spin at tremendous speed, tearing through rock, metal, and even magic-enhanced barriers with alarming ease. They produce a chilling, grinding noise that haunts the tunnels, a sound as unnerving as the sight of the green, flickering energy that arcs around the device's tips. When put into overdrive, the device is capable of tearing apart huge swaths of earth and foes alike with the thunderous roar of its whirring drill.

The hex grinder's primary function is that of an unhindered excavator. With its pair of interlocked, spiraling drills spinning at astonishing speed, the device can burrow through the toughest of materials with ease. This ability is exploited by the ratfolk to quickly create new tunnels and pathways in the underground labyrinth they call home. Using the hex grinder, they can swiftly approach their unsuspecting enemies from unexpected directions, launching devastating ambushes that often turn the tide of battle in their favor.

In the realm of siege warfare, the hex grinder is equally menacing. It can quickly undermine defensive walls, chew through gatehouses, and reduce towers to rubble, making short work of even the most formidable fortifications. When faced with a barrier, whether physical or magical, the ratfolk operators merely rev up the hex grinder and let it do its terrifying work. In a matter of moments, once impregnable defenses crumble, sowing chaos among the defenders and paving the way for the ratfolk's vicious onslaught.



\columnbreak

>
> ***Fire (Leader Action).*** If the team leader is Medium or Small sized, it gains a burrow speed of 15 ft until the end of its turn. It can also burrow through solid rock, leaving a 5-foot-wide, 5-foot-high tunnel in its wake. Once during the leader's turn, while it is part of the weapons team, it may attempt to use the drill against a target within 5 feet of it, forcing the target to make a DC 15 Dexterity saving throw. On a failed save, the target takes 19 (3d12) piercing damage and 13 (4d8) thunder damage, and is knocked prone if it is a creature. Objects and structures take double damage.

If the ground in that area is made of earth or stone, it becomes difficult terrain until cleared.
>
> At the end of the turn, the leader must roll to check for a Mishap.

> 
> If the safety protocol has been overridden, the burrow speed increases to 30 feet, and instead of using the drill against a single target within 5 feet, the leader can target each creature and structure in a 15-foot cube originating from the weapon and touching the ground, forcing them all to make the saving throw against the drill's effect. If the ground in that area is made of earth or stone, it becomes difficult terrain until cleared.
>
> At the end of the turn, the leader must roll to check for a Mishap.

\columnbreak

<br>

##### Hex Grinder Mishap Table
| d6  |    Mishap Name               | Mishap Effect             |   Repair Check Type           |
|:----:|:---------------------:| :-------------------------:| :-----------------:|
| 1    | Cave-in! | Any tunnels created by the weapon within 30 feet of its location collapse. Creatures inside these tunnels must make a DC Strength saving throw. On a failed save, a creature takes 36 (8d8) bludgeoning damage and becomes buried. On a successful save, it takes half as much damage but still becomes buried. <br> A buried creature is blinded, restrained, and has total cover. The creature gains 1 level of exhaustion for every 5 minutes it remains buried. It can attempt to dig itself free as an action by making a Strength check, with advantage if it has a burrow speed. <br> On a successful check, the creature is no longer blinded or restrained and can move up to half its speed through the collapsed tunnel area until the end of its turn. However, if it ends its turn within the collapsed tunnel area, it must make the check again or risk becoming buried again. A creature that fails this check three times can no longer attempt to dig itself out. <br> An unburied creature can spend 1 minute freeing a buried creature if it knows approximately where the buried creature is located within the debris. | none
| 2-3 &emsp;&emsp;    |Broken Shock Absorbers| Until this mishap ends, any creature that starts its turn as a member of the weapons team is knocked prone.| Str
| 4-5    | Energy Loss | Until this mishap ends, the burrow speed it granted by the Fire function is reduced by 20 feet, and it no longer deals thunder damage to creatures that fail saving throws against its effect. |  Dex
| 6    | Power Down | The weapon's functions can't be used until this mishap ends. | Str

\pagebreakNum




#### Hex Grinder Upgrades

You can apply any of the following upgrades to a hex grinder. Doing so increases its CR by 1 per upgrade applied.


**Seismic Snare.** When a creature fails the saving throw against the weapon's Fire function and is standing on earth or stone, it becomes buried as it sinks into the ground. A buried creature is restrained. Any creature, including the buried one, can use its action to free the buried creature by succeeding on a Strength check against the weapon's DC. This check has advantage if the creature making it has a burrow speed.

**Emboldening Fumes.** When the Fire function is used, each creature that is part of the weapons team gains 10 temporary hit points at the end of the turn. While a creature has these temporary hit points, it is poisoned and immune to being frightened or charmed. A creature immune to the poisoned condition cannot gain these temporary hit points. If the weapon's safety protocol has been overridden, the team gains 20 temporary hit points instead. If the weapon has a Mishap, they gain 30 temporary hit points instead.

**Hex-Quake.** Whenever a creature fails its saving throw against the weapon's Fire function while standing on difficult terrain created by any hex-grinder within the last minute, it takes an extra 13(2d12) plus 9(2d8) thunder damage.

#### Hex Grinder Tactics

The hex grinder weapons teams expertly lead ratfolk in subterranean ambushes and serve as formidable shock troopers.

The hex grinder should be part of preplanned ambush teams, bursting from the ground to surprise enemies. However, the emergence point might be slightly random due to the difficulty of pinpoint precision during emergence. Note that the tunnels may require Medium creatures to squeeze through for traversal, except for ratfolk, who can easily navigate them with their Crevice Crawler feature.


\columnbreak

To determine if the hex grinder surprises enemies, have the weapons team carrying it perform Stealth checks. The team should override the safety protocol to move at maximum speed just before reaching the surface, preventing enemies from preparing for battle if they notice the incoming attack.

Upon surfacing, the team targets the nearest high-armor and low-dexterity enemy with the weapons Fire ability. If they can hit multiple targets without causing too much harm to friendly forces, they will override the safety protocol and use the area-of-effect version of the Fire ability. This will provide advantage to attacking allies if the targets are knocked prone. The difficult terrain created by this ability can also facilitate escape or hinder enemy reinforcements.

The burrowing ability remains useful even after surfacing. It allows the weapons team to move through the difficult terrain they create, avoid movement penalties, dig underground to dodge ranged attacks, and escape against Medium-sized creatures more easily.

##### Hex Grinder Upgrade Tactics
&emsp;**Seismic Snare.** This upgrade enhances the hex grinder's debuffing capability, making it an excellent choice when teaming up with groups of ratfolk.

**Emboldening Fumes.** This upgrade empowers the hex grinder to be far more daring. Those affected by the fumes will never flee from battle.

**Hex-Quake.** This upgrade turns the team into masters of area denial. The safety protocol should be overridden whenever this feature is used. If there are no targets on difficult terrain, the team should spend its turn spreading as much difficult terrain as possible.

   <img src='https://i.ibb.co/Hqj6XJB/tmp-287-excavator.png' style='position:absolute;right:-123px;bottom:-870px;width:1060px;transform:scaleX(1)' />

<img src='https://www.gmbinder.com/images/cPPYV7h.png' style='position:absolute; top:-330px; right:-10px; width:1000px; transform:rotate(0deg); filter:  opacity(100%)  grayscale(00%)  brightness(97%) ' />

### Hexlock Jezzails
Crafted from a crude amalgamation of scavenged metal, timeworn wood, and luminescent crystals of chaotic energy mined from the deepest corners of the underworld, the hexlock jezzail is a weapon of chilling potency. It is an exceptionally long, large-bore firearm, reinforced with metal bands and an elaborate shielding mechanism for the operator.

The ammunition it fires is nothing short of terrifying. Each bullet is a small shard of the same eerie crystal that powers the hexlock jezzail, carrying a piece of raw, volatile energy within. When fired, these bullets blaze a path through the air, leaving an eerie, glowing trail before they impact with devastating force, capable of penetrating the thickest armor.

With its range and power, the hexlock jezzail is an unmatched weapon of assassination and long-range warfare. The ratfolk snipers, perched high atop their subterranean cliffs or hidden in the labyrinthine tunnels, can lay low powerful adversaries from an immense distance, their presence often only revealed by the greenish streak of a successful kill.

However, the hexlock jezzail is as dangerous to its operator as it is to its targets. The raw energy within the ammunition and the firearm itself is volatile and unstable. A jammed bullet, a malfunctioning firing mechanism, or simply overuse can lead to disastrous explosions, often fatally wounding the wielder and those around them.
___

>

>
> ***Fire (Leader Action).*** The leader fires the weapon at a target of its choice that it can see that's within 400 feet but more than 5 feet away. The target must succeed on a DC 15 Dexterity saving throw or suffer 39 (6d12) piercing damage and 15 (6d4) radiant damage. The target gains advantage on this saving throw if the leader is within 5 feet of a hostile creature or if the leader moved during its last turn.

<br>

#### Hexlock Jezzail Upgrades

You can apply any of the following upgrades to a hexlock jezzail. Doing so increases its CR by 1 per upgrade applied.

**Rat-Eye Scopes.** At the end of the team leader's turn, if they have not moved, they can choose to take aim at a creature within 400 feet that they can see. The leader maintains its aim at the target until the leader moves, or the leader can no longer see the target, or the target moves more than 400 feet away from the team leader. While the leader maintains this aim, the target has disadvantage on saving throws against the weapon's Fire function.

**Sniper Jezzail.** A creature doesn't have disadvantage on Dexterity (Stealth) checks while part of the weapons team, and creatures on the weapons team can traverse or halt in a space large enough to accommodate an object one size smaller than themselves without squeezing. Additionally, using the weapon doesn't reveal the weapons team's position to other creatures they are more than 30 feet away from.






\pagebreakNum

<br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br>

**Embedding Rounds.** When a creature fails a saving throw against the weapon's Fire ability, the bullet embeds in the target for one minute. While embedded, the creature cannot regain hit points, and at the end of each of its turns, it takes 10 (3d6) radiant damage. The target creature or another creature within 5 feet can use an action to make a DC Wisdom (Medicine) check, attempting to extract the bullet. The target creature has disadvantage on this check if it attempts to remove the bullet from itself. On a successful check, the bullet is removed; however, on a failed check, the creature suffers 10 (3d6) radiant damage.

#### Hexlock Jezzail Tactics
These weapons teams serve as snipers and prioritize targeting enemies with high armor and low dexterity. They swiftly retreat when confronted in melee combat.

#### Hexlock Jezzail Upgrade Tactics 
&emsp;**Rat-Eye Scopes.** This upgrade enhances the hexlock jezzail's sniping capabilities. The weapons team must be defended by other creatures to make effective use of this upgrade. If the team isn't near death, their weapon remains operational, and their target is still within range and appears vulnerable, they will continue firing despite sources of disadvantage. 

**Sniper Jezzail.** This upgrade allows the hexlock jezzail to carry out ambushes in places where other weapons can't. If the team uses the Scurry Away feature, they'll take their time to run until they can become hidden again before resuming fire.





\columnbreak

<br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br>

**Embedding Rounds.** While the team will still prioritize hitting low-dexterity targets, with this upgrade, they will focus on isolated targets that are unable to receive assistance in removing the bullets.

### Two-Creature Weapon Loot
Most of the valuable goods that can be looted from these weapons are materials salvaged from their remains. Salvaged material can usually be gathered using an Intelligence (Smith’s Tools) or Intelligence (Tinker’s Tools) check. Alternatively, you can roll for the loot randomly using a flat modifier.

#### Two-Creature Weapon Loot Tables
The following tables describe the number of items and value of those items the players are able to loot depending on the result of their check or the results of your roll. If they're making checks, you can have them make a separate check for each creature they're looting or use one check for multiple creatures at once to save time.

The Basic Weapon Loot Table should be used for the standard version of any of the two-creature weapons in this document. The Advanced Weapon Table should be used for the more powerful variant of any of the weapons.

##### Basic Weapon Loot Table

| Looting Check Result or 1d20 + 3 |  Loot  |
|:---:|:-----------:|
|  1-6  | 1 5gp Item & 1d6(3) 5sp Items |
|  7-11 | 1 5gp Item & 2d4(5) 5sp Items | 
|  12-17 | 1 5gp Item & 1d6(3) 1gp Items | 
|  18-21 | 1 10gp Item & 2d4(5) 1gp Items | 
|  22+ | 1 10gp Item & 3d4(7) 1gp Items | 

\columnbreak

| Looting Check Result or 1d20 + 5 |  Loot  |
|:---:|:-----------:|
|  1-8  | 1 10gp Item & 1d6(3) 1gp Items |
|  9-12 | 1 10gp Item & 2d4(5) 1gp Items | 
|  13-18 | 1 20gp Item & 1d6(3) 2gp Items | 
|  19-22 | 1 20gp Item & 2d4(5) 2gp Items | 
|  23+ | 1 20gp Item & 3d4(7) 2gp Items |

#  Siege Weapons
These weapons have been engineered for large-scale warfare against enemy armies and settlements. What sets them apart from other weapons is their size and the number of creatures required to operate them effectively (generally more than two). These weapons range from highly sophisticated cannons and rocket launchers to crude catapults and giant slingshots. Regardless of their form, they are all large enough that moving them is a slow process and labor-intensive enough to use that they require a team of creatures to operate them effectively.

## Repairing Weapons
If a weapon has taken damage but still has at least 1 hit point, a creature can spend 1 hour or more attempting to repair the damage. The creature must have the necessary tools and parts for the repairs. After 1 hour of repair work, the creature makes an Intelligence check, adding its proficiency bonus to the check if it is proficient with the required tools. If the check succeeds, the weapon regains 2d4 + the creature's Intelligence modifier + the creature's proficiency bonus hit points. If the check fails, the weapon does not regain any hit points, but the repair can be attempted again using the same tools and replacement parts.

\columnbreak

## Siege Weapon Attributes
In addition to the common attributes of size, weight, AC, HP, and damage immunity, these weapons have the following additional attributes and considerations:

### Hit Points 
A weapon has hit points that can be restored through repairs. When its hit points reach 0, the weapon becomes inoperative and irreparably damaged. 

Many weapons have a damage threshold. Any source of damage less than this threshold only inflicts superficial damage and doesn't lower the weapon's hit points.

### Weapon DC 
The weapon's DC is used whenever a creature makes a check to fix mishaps, when a creature is repairing the weapon, or the weapon forces a creature to make a saving throw.

### Challenge Rating
When players face enemies equipped with fully functioning siege weapons, the encounter's challenge rating (CR) should be calculated as if the weapon is an additional creature with its own CR.

<img src='https://i.ibb.co/JjYPNWK/Unleash-Shell-The-Brothers-War-Mt-G-Art.jpg' style='position:absolute; top:-40px; right:0px; width:820px; transform:scaleX(1)' />

<img src='https://www.gmbinder.com/images/WGybwnz.png' style='position:absolute; top:195px; right:100px; width:950px; filter:  grayscale(00%) brightness(97%); transform:rotate(10deg)' />


<img src='https://www.gmbinder.com/images/WGybwnz.png' style='position:absolute; top:249px; right:-200px; width:900px; filter:  grayscale(00%) brightness(97%); transform:rotate(0deg)' />


\pagebreakNum



### Ammo / Fuel
Weapons may require ammunition, such as bullets, or fuel, such as flammable chemicals, to make attacks. This part of the stat block includes the cost of the ammo and the number of charges it has, which represents the number of times the weapon can be used before it needs to be reloaded.

### Functions
By default, siege weapons have three different functions, which can each be activated as an action by its operators: Prep, Load, and Fire. Each function can only be performed once per round unless it states otherwise. Creatures within reach of a creature performing one of these functions can make opportunity attacks against them.

#### Prep
Siege weapons need to be prepped in different ways between being fired. This preparation could be cranking a ballista or cleaning the barrel of a cannon. Many siege weapons have multiple Prep functions that must be performed before they can be used again. In these cases, the different Prep actions can be done by different creatures within the same round. Unless stated otherwise, all the Prep functions must be completed before the weapon can be loaded.

\columnbreak

#### Load
This function is used to reload the weapon's ammunition up to its full capacity. It requires the creature loading it to have immediate access to the weapon's ammunition. If a creature doing the loading is hit by an opportunity it provoked by doing this, it drops the ammo and wastes its action.

#### Fire
This function is used to aim and fire the weapon at a target chosen by the creature performing the function.

### Passive Traits
This section describes any traits of the weapon has that don't require actions to utilize.

### Mishaps table
Some weapons can suffer a malfunction when certain functions are used. When such an event occurs, it will suffer a mishap and need to roll on its Mishap Table to determine what adverse effect it suffers. 

A creature can attempt to resolve a mishap by using its action to make an ability check based on the nature of the mishap. The creature making the check can be any member of the weapons team or anyone else within reach of the weapon. If the creature is proficient with the tools required for repairs and has them at hand, it adds its proficiency bonus to the check. A successful check ends the mishap. Mishaps that do not have a Repair Check Type cannot be repaired.

<img src='https://64.media.tumblr.com/97957bfd89fc58990ebbe31b4b543960/a95157cb330b1736-23/s1280x1920/c9807add3c7fc2bd781c456d1f8a9cee5de0f6e2.png' style='position:absolute; bottom:-40px; right:0px; width:820px; transform:scaleX(1)' />

<img src='https://www.gmbinder.com/images/cPPYV7h.png' style='position:absolute; top:-485px; right:-100px; width:1000px; transform:rotate(8deg); filter:  opacity(100%)  grayscale(00%)  brightness(97%) ' />

<img src='https://www.gmbinder.com/images/cPPYV7h.png' style='position:absolute; top:-455px; right:-200px; width:1000px; transform:rotate(-2deg); filter:  opacity(100%)  grayscale(00%)  brightness(97%) ' />

<img src='https://www.gmbinder.com/images/cPPYV7h.png' style='position:absolute; top:-451px; right:-00px; width:1000px; transform:rotate(-4deg); filter:  opacity(100%)  grayscale(00%)  brightness(97%) ' />

<br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br>

## Hex Lightning Cannons
The hex lightning wannon is a massive, wheeled contraption that bristles with crackling energy. Constructed from a combination of scavenged metal and mysterious components, the cannons are powered by a rare and volatile energy source harnessed from the raw forces of chaos. Ratfolk engineers channel this energy into the cannon's twisted mechanisms, preparing it to unleash its devastating power.

When activated, the hex lightning cannon fires lethal bolts of crackling, coruscating energy. These electrifying projectiles surge forth, capable of piercing through the toughest armor and obliterating enemy formations with explosive force. The destructive potential of the hex lightning cannon is unmatched, making it a prized asset in the ratfolk's arsenal of war machines.

However, its power is not easily controlled, and hex lightning cannons are as dangerous to their operators as they are to their enemies. The unleashed energy often surges uncontrollably, causing catastrophic feedback that can result in explosions or the cannon tearing itself apart. Only the most skilled and daring ratfolk engineers dare to operate these deadly devices, often as a testament to their ambition and thirst for power.

The ratfolk clans jealously guard the secrets of creating and operating hex lightning cannons, considering them a potent symbol of their supremacy and a means to assert dominance over their rivals. Despite the best efforts of the ratfolk, hex lightning cannons do occasionally fall into the hands of their rivals, who are quick to modify them for their own uses in war. When brought to bear on the battlefield, the eerie glow of the cannon's energy casts a chilling pall over friend and foe alike, foretelling the chaos and destruction to come.


\columnbreak

<Br>

___
> ## Hex Lightning Cannon 
> *Huge siege weapon (8,500 pounds lb.)*
> ___
> - **Weapon DC** 17
> - **Armor Class** 18 
> - **Hit Points** 150 (damage threshold: 10)
>___
> - **Damage Immunities** poison, psychic
> - **Ammo** Hex Lighting Core (6 rounds, 1,000g).
> - **Challenge** 5 (1,800 XP)
> ___
>
> ### Functions
>
> ***Load.*** The weapon is loaded with a Hex Lightning Core. This must be done before it is prepped.
>
> ***Prep (2)*** The weapon is prepped to fire its next shot. This prep must be done while it is loaded. It must be prepped two times before it can fire.
>
>
> ***Fire.*** The weapon fires a line of lightning that forms a line 4d4 x 10 feet long and 5 feet wide, which blasts out from it in the direction of user's choice. Each creature in the line must make a DC 17 Dexterity saving throw. A creature takes 36 (8d8) lightning damage on a failed save, or half as much damage on a successful one. The lightning ignites flammable objects in the area that aren't being worn or carried. If three or more of the d4s rolled have the same number, the weapon has a mishap. If it has half its health or less, it has a mishap if two or more d4s roll the same number. If a mishap occurs, resolve it before having the weapon fire.

##### Hex Lightning Mishaps
| d6  |    Mishap Name               | Mishap Effect             | 
|:----:|:---------------------:| :-----------------:| :-----------------:|
| 1   | Meltdown | The cannon explodes, preventing it from firing and destroying it. Each creature within 15 feet of it must succeed on a Dexterity saving throw or take 21 (6d8) priercing damage plus 21 (6d8) radiant damage  |
| 2-3 &emsp;&emsp;   | Electrical Feedback | The cannon takes 71 (8d8) + 35) lightning damage.|
| 4-5    | Sputtering Fizzle | The cannon does not fire and must be fully prepped again before it can be fired.|
| 6    | Energy Overload | Unfathomable energies send the cannon spinning wildly. The cannon fires in a random direction, and the length of its blast is 300 ft (no roll needed). To determine the direction, roll a d8 and assign a direction to each die face.|

> *Huge siege object (8,500 pounds lb.)*
> ___
> - **Weapon DC** 19
> - **Armor Class** 20 
> - **Hit Points** 200 (damage threshold: 10)
>___

> ___

> ### Functions
>
> ***Load.*** The weapon is loaded with a Hex Lightning Core. This must be done before it is prepped.
>
> ***Prep (2)*** The weapon is prepped to fire its next shot. This prep must be done while it is loaded. It must be prepped two times before it can fire.
>
> ***Fire.*** The weapon fires a line of lightning that forms a line 4d4 x 10 feet long and 5 feet wide, which blasts out from it in the direction of user's choice. Each creature in the line must make a DC 19 Dexterity saving throw. A creature takes 45 (10d8) lightning damage on a failed save, or half as much damage on a successful one. The lightning ignites flammable objects in the area that aren't being worn or carried. If three or more of the d4s rolled have the same number, the weapon has a mishap. If it has half its health or less, it has a mishap if two or more d4s roll the same number. If a mishap occurs, resolve it before having the weapon fire.

\columnbreak



### Hex Lightning Cannon Upgrades

You can apply any of the following upgrades to a hex lightning cannon. Doing so increases its CR by 1 per upgrade applied.

* **Hex Conduit.** When a creature makes a saving throw against the cannon's Fire function due to being in the area of its lightning, all other creatures within 5 feet of that creature must also make the saving throw against the effect as the electricity arcs between them. This arcing causes the original creature, and everyone the lightning arced to, to suffer disadvantage on their saving throws.
* **Regenerating Radiation.** When a creature preps or loads the cannon, it must make a DC 15 Constitution saving throw (which it can choose to fail). On a failed save, it gains a level of exhaustion and regains 15 hit points. A creature immune to exhaustion cannot gain hit points this way.
* **Hex Stone Dynamos.** The cannon no longer experiences mishaps when rolling for the length of its lightning blast. Instead, when the cannon rolls for the length of the line, it gains a charge for each 4 rolled on a d4 that lasts one minute. The cannon deals an additional 4 (1d8) damage per charge it has. However, if the weapon ever gains 4 or more charges, it suffers the Energy Overload Mishap. This mishap causes the cannon to take 71 (8d8) + 35 lightning damage and lose all its charges. If reduced to 0 hit points this way, the cannon experiences the Meltdown mishap.

   <img src='https://i.ibb.co/VJn3yf2/consulate-turret.png' style='position:absolute;right:0px;bottom:-60px;width:860px;transform:scaleX(-1)' />

<img src='https://www.gmbinder.com/images/cPPYV7h.png' style='position:absolute; top:-440px; right:-10px; width:1000px; transform:rotate(0deg); filter:  opacity(100%)  grayscale(00%)  brightness(97%) ' />

\pagebreakNum

### Hex Lightning Cannon Tactics

The hex lightning cannon serves as a powerful piece of artillery. Unlike many other artillery pieces, it fires in a straight line, which means that allied troops in front of it must clear a path for its lightning blast. Alternatively, the crew can choose to fire through expendable allies to reach prime enemy targets. Bogging down foes in such allies can be an effective way to ensure they can't escape the cannon's blasts.

#### Hex Lightning Cannon Upgrade Tactics

**Hex Conduit.** This upgrade is particularly useful when there are many expendable units on the front line. These additional bodies can be utilized to impose disadvantage on enemies' saving throws by triggering the arcing lightning effect.

**Regenerating Radiation.** This upgrade works best with expendable, less capable creatures working the cannon, as it keeps them alive but limits their combat effectiveness. However, its usefulness diminishes when the crew is more proficient in combat, as engaging with foes directly can be used as a last resort if the cannon becomes inoperable for some reason.

**Hex Stone Dynamos.** This upgrade turns the weapon into a truly chaotic device. The predictability of its operations can be drastically reduced, leading to unforeseen outcomes on the battlefield.

\columnbreak

##### Hex Lightning Cannon Adventure Hooks

| d4 | Plot Hook |
|:---:|:-----------:|
|  1  | **Unstable Power:** Reports surface of a rogue hex lightning cannon that has fallen into the hands of an unscrupulous warlord. However, the cannon's energy source has been tampered with, causing it to emit uncontrollable and increasingly unstable bursts of hex energy. The players are hired to neutralize the cannon and prevent a catastrophic explosion that could devastate nearby settlements. As they close in on the warlord's stronghold, they must contend with the cannon's erratic power and the warlord's minions fiercely guarding their newfound weapon. |
|  2  |**The Forbidden Auction:** Rumors spread of a clandestine auction where dangerous and forbidden weapons, including a fully operational hex lightning cannon, are up for sale to the highest bidder. The players' attention is drawn to this dark gathering when they learn that rival factions and hostile nations are sending representatives. The adventurers must infiltrate the auction, posing as buyers, to prevent these deadly weapons from falling into the wrong hands.  |
|  3 |**Do The Time Warp:** During a fierce battle, a hex lightning cannon suffers a meltdown that triggers a temporal anomaly. The players find themselves trapped in a pocket of time that repeats the battle over and over. Each time the loop resets, they must learn from their mistakes and find a way to prevent the cannon from causing the temporal disruption.|
|  4  |**Capturing Lightning:** The players find themselves fighting on a wartorn battlefield against a ratfolk army, attempting to defeat a group of ratfolk who have secured a key position using a hex lighting cannon. As the players battle the ratfolk operating the cannon, overwhelming amounts of ratfolk reinforcements arrive, and the players must secure the cannon so they can use it to blast apart verminous soldiers. |

Most of the valuable goods that can be looted from these weapons are materials salvaged from their remains. # Self-Propelled Vehicles
Most land vehicles in fantasy settings are pulled by other creatures, such as wagons, carriages, or chariots. However, through some combination of technology or magic, some vehicles may be self-propelled and driven by a passenger. These may be relatively small mechanical contraptions, magically self-propelled carriages, or mighty war machines rumbling across blasted battlefields. 

The following rules can help you codify how to use these vehicle types in your games. They can be applied to vehicles of different shapes and sizes and used as tools for designing your own vehicles. The rules here can be applied to most self-powered vehicles piloted by a passenger. 

## Self-Propelled Vehicle Rules
Self-propelled vehicles are vehicles able to move without needing to be pushed or pulled by another creature, and they usually don’t need an external energy source (such as wind). Throughout this document, they will be referred to simply as vehicles. Creatures within a vehicle are referred to as passengers. 
In combat, vehicles use most of the same rules as creatures, with the following additional considerations:

### Opportunity Attacks
Vehicles provoke opportunity attacks as usual. When a vehicle provokes an opportunity attack, the attacker can target the vehicle itself or any creature riding on or inside it, provided they are within reach and do not have total cover.



\columnbreak

### Spacing Within Vehicles
All creatures within a vehicle count as being within 5 feet of each other.


### Entering and Exiting Vehicles
Entering or exiting the vehicle costs a creature half of its movement. Each creature inside the vehicle may use its reaction to make an opportunity attack against the creature entering or exiting.


### Crashing into Creatures and Objects
A vehicle can crash into a creature or object by entering its space. When it does, the creature or object must make a Dexterity or Strength saving throw (the target's choice) using the vehicle's DC. On a failed save, the target takes 1d6 bludgeoning damage for every 10 feet the vehicle moved in a straight line before attempting to enter the target's space (maximum 20d6 damage).

If the target is a creature, it is also knocked prone. On a successful Dexterity save, the target takes no damage and is not knocked prone. On a successful Strength save, the creature takes half damage, is not knocked prone, and the vehicle's speed becomes 0 until the end of the turn. A target can only make this saving throw once per turn.

If the vehicle is at least two size categories larger than the target it crashed into, it can continue moving through the target's space if it has any movement remaining. Otherwise, the vehicle comes to a sudden stop. If the target is an impassable object that could reasonably damage the vehicle, such as an iron wall, the vehicle comes to a sudden stop and takes 1d6 bludgeoning damage for every 10 feet it moved since its last turn (maximum 20d6 damage). Each creature on or inside the vehicle takes the damage as well

<img src='https://i.ibb.co/7VQV8VK/ballista-charger.png' style='position:absolute; top:-0px; right:0px; width:817px; transform:scaleX(1)' />

<img src='https://www.gmbinder.com/images/WGybwnz.png' style='position:absolute; top:45px; right:100px; width:950px; filter:  grayscale(00%) brightness(97%); transform:rotate(4deg)' />


<img src='https://www.gmbinder.com/images/WGybwnz.png' style='position:absolute; top:100px; right:-200px; width:900px; filter:  grayscale(00%) brightness(97%); transform:rotate(0deg)' />

\pagebreakNum

### Prone Vehicles
If vehicle falls prone, it cannot right itself and is incapacitated until it is flipped upright.

### Falling Vehicles
When a vehicle falls from a height of 10 feet or higher, it and all creatures on or inside it take damage from the fall as normal and land in a prone position. If the vehicle falls due to the actions of its driver (such as jumping off a ramp) it may not land prone (DM’s discretion) but still takes fall damage.



### Repairing Vehicles
If a vehicle has taken damage but still has at least 1 hit point, a creature can spend 1 hour or more attempting to repair the damage. The vehicle must be stationary, and the creature must have the necessary tools and parts for the repairs. After 1 hour of repair work, the creature makes an Intelligence check, adding its proficiency bonus to the check if it is proficient with the tools required for the repairs. If the check succeeds, the vehicle regains 2d4 + its Intelligence modifier + its proficiency bonus hit points. If the check fails, the vehicle does not regain any hit points, but the repair can be attempted again using the same tools and replacement parts.

### Vehicular Exhaustion 
Certain circumstances can cause a vehicle to malfunction and eventually break down due to wear and tear. This wear and tear can be represented using exhaustion rules, as described in Appendix A of the Player's Handbook, with the following modifications:

* When a vehicle reaches exhaustion level 6, its hit points drop to 0, and the vehicle breaks down.
* The only way to remove the effects of exhaustion on a vehicle is through repair. This can be done using the <br> rules described in the Repairing Vehicles section <br> above. If the attempt to repair the vehicle <br> succeeds, the vehicle's exhaustion level <br> decreases by 1. If the check fails, the <br> vehicle's exhaustion level remains <br> unchanged, but the repair attempt <br> can be made again using <br> the same tools and <br> replacement parts.

\columnbreak

## Self-Propelled Vehicle Attributes
Besides the size, weight, AC, HP, and damage immunity attributes common to all objects, these vehicles have the following additional attributes and considerations:

### Hit Points 
A vehicle's hit points can be restored through vehicle repairs. However, when a vehicle's hit points reach 0, it becomes inoperative and is irreparably damaged.
### Damage Threshold
Most vehicles possess bulk or armor that enables them to withstand minor hits. A vehicle with a damage threshold is immune to all damage unless the amount of damage it takes is equal to or greater than its damage threshold value. In such cases, the vehicle takes damage as usual. Damage that fails to meet or exceed the vehicle's damage threshold is considered superficial and does not reduce the vehicle's hit points.

### Mishap Threshold
When a vehicle sustains damage from a single source that is equal to or exceeds its mishap threshold, it is required to roll on the Mishaps table (refer to the Mishaps section).

<img src='https://i.ibb.co/pZzQTPR/surgehacker-mech.png' style='position:absolute; bottom:-100px; right:-200px; width:1016px; transform:scaleX(-1)' />

<img src='https://www.gmbinder.com/images/cPPYV7h.png' style='position:absolute; top:-410px; right:-170px; width:1000px; transform:rotate(0deg); filter:  opacity(100%)  grayscale(00%)  brightness(97%) ' />

<img src='https://www.gmbinder.com/images/cPPYV7h.png' style='position:absolute; top:-300px; right:105px; width:1000px; transform:rotate(-37deg); filter:  opacity(100%)  grayscale(00%)  brightness(97%) ' />

<img src='https://www.gmbinder.com/images/cPPYV7h.png' style='position:absolute; top:-451px; right:-00px; width:1000px; transform:rotate(-4deg); filter:  opacity(100%)  grayscale(00%)  brightness(97%) ' />

\pagebreakNum

### Creature Capacity 
Creature capacity determines the number of creatures that can ride the vehicle comfortably. Additional creatures can fit by squeezing or clinging to the outside of the vehicle.

### Cargo Capacity
Cargo capacity indicates the maximum weight of cargo the vehicle can carry.

### Vehicle DC 
Whenever the vehicle requires a creature to make a check or saving throw, it uses this number as the DC.

### Challenge Rating
When players face enemies that are equipped with a fully functioning vehicle, the challenge rating (CR) of the encounter should be calculated as if the vehicle is an additional creature with its own CR.

### Ability Scores 
A vehicle possesses the standard six ability scores that creatures have, along with their corresponding modifiers. The Strength of the vehicle is determined by its size and weight, while Dexterity represents its handling and maneuverability. The Constitution of a vehicle reflects its durability and quality of construction. In most cases, vehicles have a score of 0 in Intelligence, Wisdom, and Charisma.

If a vehicle has a score of 0 in a particular ability score, it automatically fails any ability check or saving throw that relies on that score.

### Action Stations
A vehicle may have one or more Action Stations. Each of these stations requires a certain number of creatures to operate and may grant those creatures some amount of cover. The creatures operating these stations must be passengers within the vehicle, but not all passengers need to be operating a station. A creature operating a station <br> can use an action to activate the station's effect.  <br> A station can be occupied by only one <br> creature at a time and can only <br> be activated once per round. 

\columnbreak

#### The Helm 
Most vehicles that must be piloted by a passenger (referred to as the driver) have an Action Station known as the Helm, where the vehicle's movement is controlled. It usually consists of a chair equipped with a wheel, levers, pedals, and other controls. If a vehicle has a helm with no one operating it, it automatically fails Dexterity saving throws. A driver who is proficient with land vehicles can add their proficiency bonus to ability checks and saving throws made using the vehicle's ability scores.

The driver can use an action to propel the vehicle up to its speed or bring it to a complete stop. While the vehicle is in motion, the driver can steer it along any desired course. If the driver becomes incapacitated, leaves the helm, or takes no action to alter the vehicle's course and speed, the vehicle will continue moving in the same direction and at the same speed as it did during the driver's last turn until it collides with an obstacle large enough to stop its movement.


### Mishaps
Most vehicles have a Mishaps Table, which describes different ways its functionality can go awry under adverse conditions. When certain abilities or conditions dictate, roll on this Mishaps Table. 

To resolve a Mishap, a creature can use its action to make an ability check based on the nature of the mishap (refer to the Mishaps section). If the vehicle is moving, the check is made with disadvantage. If the creature is proficient with the tools required for the repairs and has them at hand, it adds its proficiency bonus to the check. A successful check ends the mishap. Mishaps that do not have a Repair Check Type cannot be repaired.



<img src='https://i.ibb.co/VtKTs6t/Dermotaxi-Modern-Horizons-2-Mt-G-Art-1024x786.jpg' style='position:absolute; bottom:-195px; right:-0px; width:816px; transform:scaleX(-1);filter:opacity(100%);'/>

 <img src='https://www.gmbinder.com/images/cPPYV7h.png' 
  style='position:absolute;right:-100px;top:-395px;height:1400px;width:1416px;transform:rotate(-0deg)' />

 <img src='https://www.gmbinder.com/images/cPPYV7h.png' 
  style='position:absolute;right:-50px;top:-300px;height:1400px;width:1416px;transform:rotate(-28deg)' />

\pagebreakNum

<br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br>

## Doom Shredders
The doom shredders are imposing contraptions, reminiscent of giant, twisted cogs that screech and grind as they surge forward. Propelled by their spinning wheels, the vehicles possess incredible speed, allowing them to swiftly close in on their foes, leaving chaos and destruction in their wake.

Mounted on each doom shredder is a skilled ratfolk driver, operating the complex controls and piloting the vehicle with unmatched precision. The doom shredders are often deployed in the vanguard of ratfolk armies, charging into enemy lines with ruthless efficiency. 



\columnbreak

<br><br><br><br><br>

Armed with gnashing blades and deadly weapons, they eagerly carve a path through enemy ranks, dismembering all who dare stand in their way.

However, despite their formidable strength, the doom shredders are not without their risks. The unstable combination of engineering and sorcery makes them unpredictable, and accidents or malfunctions can result in catastrophic consequences, claiming the lives of both their operators and enemies alike.

##### Doom Shredder Mishaps
| d6  |    Mishap Name               | Mishap Effect             |   Repair Check Type            |
|:----:|:---------------------:| :-----------------:| :-----------------:|
| 1    | Generator Explosion | The vehicle is destroyed, and each creature within 15 feet of it must make a DC Dexterity saving throw, taking 18 (4d8) piercing damage plus 18 (4d8) radiant damage on a failure.  |None
| 2-3 &emsp;&emsp;    | Electrical Short |  Any creature that starts its turn on or inside the vehicle takes 10 (3d6) lightning damage at the start of its turn until this mishap ends.| Str
| 4-5    | Blade Jam | The doom shredder's blades stop rotating. It loses its Whirling Death feature and any upgrades it has until the mishap ends.| Str
| 6    |  Power Failure. | The vehicle's speed becomes 0 until the mishap ends.  | Dex

> - **Damage Immunities** poison, psychic
> - **Condition Immunities** blinded, charmed, deafened, frightened, 
paralyzed, petrified, poisoned, stunned, unconscious
> - **Challenge** 3 (700 XP)
> ___
>
> ***Heavy Set.*** The doom shredder cannot be shoved, and it has advantage on saving throws against being knocked prone.
>
> ***Unstable Design.*** When the doom shredder crashes into a creature, if it moved at least 20 feet in a straight line before impact, it rolls a d6. If the result of the d6 is a 1, the doom shredder has a mishap. If it moved 40 in a straight line before crashing, it rolls 2d6 instead and uses the lowest roll.
>
> ***Whirling Death.*** The doom shredder deals 7 (2d6) damage slashing damage instead of 3 (1d6) bludgeoning damage per 10 feet it moves in a straight line before crashing into a creature or object. If a creature fails the saving throw by 10 or more (DC 5) and the doom shredder moved at least 40 feet before crashing into the target, it cuts off one of the target's limbs at random (roll a die with a number of sides equal to the target's number of limbs; see pg. 272 of the DMG for rules on losing a limb). If the creature has no limbs to sever, it cuts off a portion of the target's body instead. A creature is immune to this effect if it is immune to slashing damage. 
>
>
> ### Action Stations
>
> ***Helm (Requires 1 Crew and Grants Three-Quarters Cover).*** Drive and steer the doom shredder.
>

> ***Heavy Set.*** The doom shredder cannot be shoved, and it has advantage on saving throws against being knocked prone.
>
> ***Unstable Design.*** When the doom shredder crashes into a creature, if it moved at least 20 feet in a straight line before impact, it rolls a d6. If the result of the d6 is a 1, the doom shredder has a mishap. If it moved 40 in a straight line before crashing, it rolls 2d6 instead and uses the lowest roll.
>
> ***Whirling Death.*** The doom shredder deals 10 (3d6) damage slashing damage instead of 3 (1d6) bludgeoning damage per 10 feet it moves in a straight line before crashing into a creature or object. If a creature fails the saving throw by 10 or more (DC 7) and the doom shredder moved at least 40 feet before crashing into the target, it cuts off one of the target's limbs at random (roll a die with a number of sides equal to the target's number of limbs; see pg. 272 of the DMG for rules on losing a limb). If the creature has no limbs to sever, it cuts off a portion of the target's body instead. A creature is immune to this effect if it is immune to slashing damage.

##### Doom Shredder Adventure Hooks

| d4  | Plot Hook |
|:---:|:-----------:|
|  1  | **Tunnel Raiders:** A ratfolk clan has begun deploying doom shredder riders to terrorize underground settlements, raid them for supplies, and weaken their defenses in preparation for larger attacks. The vehicles surge through the tunnels, leaving destruction in their wake. The adventurers have been hired to put a stop to this menace.|
|  2  |**Death Derby:** A powerful and eccentric artificer has issued a challenge to ratfolk engineers and sorcerers from all clans, inviting them to participate in a deadly race where they must pilot doom shredders to claim a legendary prize. The adventurers are drawn into this competition, facing off against other participants in a perilous race through treacherous tunnels and ruins. |
|  3 | **Blades For Sale:** A ratfolk engineer living in a scrapyard has started piecing together hex flayers and selling them to criminal gangs. The adventurers are tasked with finding where these deadly vehicles are coming from and putting a stop to their distribution.|
|  4  |**The Vermin Riders:** A gang of doom shredder riding ratfolk led by a eldritch engineer is raiding the countryside, constantly looking for fuel and upgrades for their deadly vehicles. The players are tasked with tracking them down and putting a stop to their rampage. |


### Doom Shredder Upgrades

You can apply any of the following upgrades to a doom shredder. Doing so increases its CR by 1 per upgrade applied.

**Armour-Shredding Blades.** When a creature is rammed by the doom shredder and fails the saving throw against the effect, any armor the creature is wearing is damaged and takes a permanent and cumulative -1 penalty to the AC it offers. The armor is destroyed if the penalty reduces its AC to 10. A creature can remove the -1 penalty from the armor over an hour if it has the appropriate tools and proficiency with them (blacksmith tools or leatherworker's tools, depending on the armor).

**Black Hole Reactor.** A crew member at the doom shredder's helm can use their action to activate its Black Hole Reactor. If they do so, they can use half of their movement to immediately exit the doom shredder, allowing the doom shredder to move in a straight line up to its movement speed after they do so. At the start of the creature's next turn, the doom shredder is destroyed, and each creature within 15 feet must make a DC Dexterity saving throw. On a failure, creatures take 9 (2d8) force damage for every 10 feet the doom shredder moved in a straight line during the last round. If this damage reduces the target to 20 hit points or fewer and they failed the saving throw, they are banished to another plane of existence at the DM's choice.

**Repelling Knife-Blades.** At the end of a crew member's turn, if the doom shredder moved 20 feet or more that turn, ranged attacks against the doom shredder and its crew have disadvantage until the end of that crew member's next turn.



\pagebreakNum

### Doom Shredder Tactics

Doom shredders function as hard-hitting chariots for ratfolk armies, lingering along enemy flanks until they identify a vulnerable target, then charging in to slice up their victims. Their ratfolk drivers typically use the Scurry Away trait to avoid counterattacks, driving to a safe distance before returning for another charge.

#### Doom Shredder Upgrade Tactics

&emsp;**Armour-Shredding Blades.** Pilots of doom shredders with this upgrade will specifically target armored enemies.

**Black Hole Reactor.** If the battle isn't going in the ratfolk's favor, it can activate the Black Hole Reactor as a last-ditch gambit. Note that even on the turn the ratfolk abandons the vehicle, the unmanned vehicle can still be used to crash into a target as it drives in a straight line toward its destination before detonating.

**Repelling Knife-Blades.** With this upgrade, the doom shredder's driver no longer needs to fear the repercussions of entering within range of heavy ranged fire. This makes the doom shredder perfect for harassing enemies with such attacks.

### Doom Shredder Weapon Loot
Most of the valuable goods that can be looted from this vehicle are materials salvaged from its remains. Salvaged material can usually be gathered using an Intelligence (Smith’s Tools) or Intelligence (Tinker’s Tools) check. Alternatively, you can roll for the loot randomly using a flat modifier.

#### Two-Creature Weapon Loot Tables
The following tables describe the number of items and value of those items the players are able to loot depending on the result of their check or the results of your roll. If they're making checks, you can have them make a separate check for each creature they're looting or use one check for multiple creatures at once to save time.

The Basic Weapon Loot Table should be used for the standard version of any of the two-creature weapons in this document. The Advanced Weapon Table should be used for the more powerful variant of any of the weapons.

##### Doom Shredder Loot Table

| Looting Check Result or 1d20 + 3 |  Loot  |
|:---:|:-----------:|
|  1-6  | 1 5gp Item & 1d6(3) 5sp Items |
|  7-11 | 1 5gp Item & 2d4(5) 5sp Items | 
|  12-17 | 1 5gp Item & 1d6(3) 1gp Items | 
|  18-21 | 1 10gp Item & 2d4(5) 1gp Items | 
|  22+ | 1 10gp Item & 3d4(7) 1gp Items |

## Vermin Wheels

In the sprawling laboratories of the ratfolk, technological and magical prowess intertwine in frenetic chaos. Amidst this interplay, one invention stands as a testament to the insanity and genius of the ratfolk engineers - the vermin wheel.

The vermin wheel is an immense vehicle that looms over the battlefield like a nightmarish mockery of a rat wheel, a testament to the raw and unbridled power the ratfolk engineers can command. An engineer, picked from the most daring (or unhinged) of their kind, steers the vermin wheel from a pilot seat within, guiding this deadly contraption with mad glee, careening wildly across the landscape.

The vermin wheel’s motion is powered by an army of irradiated rats, feverishly running in unison along the inside of its massive. Dangerous arcane stones built into the machine mutate and transform these rats into tireless, monstrous variants of their kin, their muscles bulging with unnatural strength and their eyes glowing an eerie green. The ceaseless running of these mutant rats drives the huge wheel, causing it to spin with a relentless, unstoppable momentum.

But the arcane stones serve a dual purpose. As the wheel spins, it generates a kind of eldritch energy, harnessed by the embedded stone. The magical mineral, imbued with the raw force of movement, channels this power into devastating blasts of arcane lightning. This energy is unleashed upon the ratfolk’s enemies in brilliant, lethal arcs, turning the vermin wheel into a rolling generator of destructive force.

> - **Damage Immunities** poison, psychic.
