> ___
> ***Fragile Cargo.*** Whenever ratfolk suffers a critical hit or is reduced to 0 hit points, it shatters a toxic wind globe centered on itself.
>
> ***Keen Smell.*** The ratfolk has advantage on Wisdom (Perception) checks that rely on smell.
>
> ***Overwhelming Mass x1.*** The first time each turn that the ratfolk hits a creature with an attack, it deals an extra 1 damage per ally it has within 5 feet of its target that isn't incapacitated. The ratfolk can benefit from up to 3 allies this way.
>
> ***Hazmat Gear.*** The ratfolk has advantage on saving throws against being poisoned.
> <Br><Br>
> ### Actions
>
> ***Multiattack.*** The ratfolk makes two dagger attacks. It can replace one attack with toxic wind globe throw.
>
> ***Dagger.*** *Melee or Ranged Weapon Attack:* +4 to hit, reach 5 ft. or range 20/60 ft., one target. *Hit:* 4 (1d4 + 2) piercing damage.
>
> ***Toxic Wind Globe (3/day)*** If ratfolk is not restrained or grappled, it can hurl the globe at a point it can see within 30 feet. The globe shatters at this point, it releases a cloud of poison gas in a 5-foot radius sphere, heavily obscuring the area. The cloud lasts for one round or until a wind of moderate or greater speed (at least 10 miles per hour) disperses it.
>
> When a creature enters an area covered by one or more of these gas clouds for the first time on a turn or starts its turn in one or more gas clouds, that creature must make a DC 13 Constitution saving throw. On a failed save, the creature takes 12 (2d8 + 3) poison damage and is poisoned until the end of its next turn. On a successful save, the creature takes half as much damage and isn’t poisoned.
>
> When ratfolk attempts to throw the globe, creatures can use their reaction to make attacks of opportunity against it as though ratfolk moved out of their reach. If a creature hits the ratfolk this way, it drops the globe, and it shatters at it's location.
>
> ### Reactions
>
> ***Scurry Away.***  When an enemy the ratfolk can see ends its turn, the ratfolk can move up to half its speed away from the creature and become frightened of it until the end of the creature's next turn. This movement doesn't provoke opportunity attacks. While frightened this way, the ratfolk can only take the Dash, Disengage, Dodge, or Hide action. This feature ignores immunity to the frightened condition.

### Doom Globe Bombardiers

The doom globe bombardiers, the elite cadre of the ratfolk's poisoned-wind infantry, represent the pinnacle of alchemical warfare. Known among their kin as the harbingers of annihilation, they are surrounded by an air of dread and respect, born out of their deadly expertise and the horrifying effectiveness of their weaponry.

The doom globes they carry are a testament to their terrifying alchemical skills. Larger and more intricately constructed than regular toxic wind globes, these lethal weapons contain concentrated concoctions of the deadliest gases known to ratfolk alchemy. A single doom globe can release a cloud of poisonous gas so vast and deadly that it can wipe out an entire battalion.

Doom globe bombardiers are often assigned critical missions that require the complete eradication of enemy forces or to breach heavily fortified positions. Despite their elite status, bombardiers are still viewed with a certain amount of trepidation by their peers. The deadly potency of their globes and the high casualty rate in their ranks serves as a constant reminder of the thin line they tread between life and death.

\columnbreak

##### Toxic Wind Bombardier Adventure Hooks
| d4  | Plot Hook |
|:---:|:-----------:|
|  1  | **The Green Fog:** A mysterious green fog has started to appear in a city at night, causing the residents to fall ill. The party must track down the source of the fog and put a stop to the bombardiers spreading it.|
|  2  |**The Toxic Trade:** The party learns of a black market operation trading in highly toxic substances. Tracking down the source reveals a group of toxic wind bombardiers producing and selling their deadly concoctions to the highest bidder. |
|  3  | **The Sewer Scourge:** People are going missing in a city's sewer system, and those that return tell tales of choking green clouds. The party must traverse the dark, winding tunnels to exterminate the bombardiers that have taken up residence there.|
|  4  |**Choked Castle:** A castle under siege from within! Ratfolk have infiltrated the castle and are using their poisoned globes to gradually force the residents into submission. The party is tasked with retaking the castle and neutralizing the toxic threat. |

### Toxic Wind Bombardier Tactics  
The toxic wind bombardiers play a crucial role in disrupting enemy groups by acting as debuffers and providing cover for their army. They achieve this by deploying poison gas clouds to blind their opponents. While they are resistant effects of the poison wind orbs they handle, they still exercise caution. Close combat is avoided, as any melee attack could shatter the orbs before they are thrown. To prevent such mishaps, they prefer to keep at least 30 feet from their targets while hurling the orbs, employing the Devious Bombardier ability to maintain this distance effectively.

When an opponent is severely injured and poisoned, and the bombardiers have numerical superiority, they may decide to move in and switch to dagger attacks.

It's important that other ratfolk avoid close proximity to toxic wind bombardiers due to the fear of a globe accidentally shattering. Even when fighting in a group, multiple toxic wind bombardiers spread out from each other, converging only when preparing to engage in melee combat.

### Toxic Wind Bombardier Loot
Because ratfolk are humanoids, most of the valuable goods that can be looted from them are the remains of the equipment they were using or valuables they were carrying or hiding nearby. Most of the challenge of looting ratfolk engineers is identifying what equipment they're carrying still has any functional value. They may also drop toxic wind globes the players can collect for their own use or sale to black market vendors. They may also drop toxic wind globes the players can collect for their own use or sale to black market vendors. You can track the globes as the ratfolk use them and allow players to loot any unused globes if they can defeat the bombardiers before they're all shattered.

Finding valuables can be done using an **Intelligence (Investigation)** or **Wisdom (Perception)** check, depending on the circumstance. 

#### Eldritch Engineer Loot Tables
The following tables describe the number of items and value of those items the players are able to loot depending on the result of their check or the results of your roll. If they're making checks, you can have them make a separate check for each creature they're looting or use one check for multiple creatures at once to save time.

## Ratfolk Soldiers & Seers
The following creatures represent the ratfolk who make up the bulk of their combat-ready forces, including their martial and mystical leadership.

### Ratfolk Chieftains
These ratfolk occupy some of the highest positions of authority within their society. Chieftans are accomplished warriors and commanders who often command smaller groups of ratfolk within a clan. They usually answer to a more powerful warlord who may have several chieftains at his command. Though they must obey their commander without question, chieftains usually rule their given domain with absolute authority and quickly quash any potential usurpers. By the same token, chieftains usually eye the position of warlord with envy, and those who are bold and opportunistic enough will eventually make a bid for greater power. 

In combat, chieftains command other ratfolk much the same way as their warlord superiors. They possess elite training, equipment, and resolve, and their commanding presence helps keep other ratfolk from routing. As such, chieftains are often put in command of strike forces charged with dangerous missions that require higher levels of bravery than ratfolk are typically inclined to provide.

### Ratfolk Warriors

Ratfolk are a prolific, though short-lived, race. They rarely want for numbers, though few of their kind have the opportunity to develop specialized skills. In battle, ratfolk clans leverage the quantity-over-quality approach of their race to field overwhelming numbers of otherwise unremarkable troops. All healthy ratfolk are equipped with basic weapons and armor and given enough rudimentary training to put it to use. These warriors then utilize their overwhelming mass to break enemy fighters they would otherwise be unable to defeat in a one-on-one fight.

#### Volcanic Slashers

Some ratfolk clans make their underground homes in volcanic regions. They quickly learn how to utilize their fiery environment to their advantage, burrowing their homes around magma chambers that provide molten rock, useful for defending their lair with lava traps. The magma also proves useful for forging equipment, and ratfolk of these clans learn to imbue all their weapons with fiery properties. 

The warriors of these clans also prove to be much hardier and heat resilient, as those lacking these qualities don’t last long within their volcanic homes. Known as volcanic slashers, these specialty warriors combine their high fortitude with flaming weapons to burn their way across the battlefield. 

<br>

* Nezumi Shadow-Watcher, Pete Venters, Wizards of the Coast
* Seismic Mountain, Piotr Dura, Wizards of the Coast

### Ratfolk Grey Prophets

These eldritch ratfolk are born with grey or white fur and small horns that set them apart from their kin and mark them for a path of arcane greatness. They are trained to be grey prophets, the spiritual leaders of ratfolk society who serve as messengers for their verminous god. This position of divine authority allows grey prophets to remain somewhat above the petty machinations and power plays of other ratfolk, and even powerful warlords are weary of incurring the ire of a grey prophet and, by proxy, its rat god.

 The favor of the rat god is made evident through the grey prophet's devastating magical abilities. Using their ruinous magic, these ratfolk can conjure blasts of elemental magic, summon massive rat tides, or drive their allies into self-destructive battle frenzies. They are also notoriously difficult to pin down in combat, able to scurry just out of reach before unleashing their destructive magic. The protection of the rat god is ever-present, and even those able to make seemingly accurate attacks against a grey prophet will often find their strikes suddenly veer off course, or their spells lose potency just as they reach their target.

#### Art Credit
* Nighteyes the Desecrator - <br>
Jim Nelson, Wizards of the Coast

### Ratfolk Slaves

These ratfolk represent the bottom rung of their <br> society. Numerous and expendable, they are <br> responsible for the lowliest and most dangerous <br> tasks, from unskilled labor to grislily test subjects. <br> Their low quality of life and hazardous duties make <br> their lives mercifully short, and most ratfolk slaves accomplish little with the time they have. 

In battle, other ratfolk use their slaves as canon <br> fodder to bog down foes. Their expendable nature <br> means other ratfolk have few qualms about giving <br> them suicidal tasks, and ratfolk slaves are often <br> subjected to friendly fire from the spells and <br> artillery of their ratfolk “allies.” 

Despite their frail nature and inferior physical <br> abilities, these lowly ratfolk can be quite ferocious <br> when they feel they have the upper hand. They <br> relish the opportunity to be tormenters rather <br> than the tormented and will utilize every <br> underhanded tactic available to them. However, <br> these ratfolk are cowards among a race known <br> for cowardice, and the moment the fight turns <br> against them, they are prone to scurry away. <br> Ratfolk slaves who die a coward’s death are liable <br> to get one last spiteful bite in as recompense for <br> a short, meaningless life of fear and pain.

### Art Credit
* Nezumi Shortfang - Daren Bader, <Br>Wizards of the Coast

<br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br>

### Ratfolk War Vermin


These ratfolk soldiers are the most massive and elite of their kind. Future war vermin are identified at a young age by their clan as their size, aggressiveness, and dark fur easily distinguish them from the rest of their litter. They are then raised via brutal training regiments designed to shape them into elite warriors. Packs of war vermin are given the best equipment in the clan and go on to serve as heavy infantry and personal retinues for powerful ratfolk commanders.

<br><br>

In combat, war vermin are less prone to the cowardice of most rat folk soldiers. Their higher resolve and heavy armor allow them to hold the line against enemy combatants, and their size, training, and deadly weaponry allow them to cut a swath through most ordinary soldiers. Thus, war vermin are often charged with protecting critical locations and individuals or leading rallying charges against particularly imposing foes.

\pagebreakNum



#### Council Guard
These albino war vermin are the most elite bodyguards in the ratfolks' under-empire. Though their origin is unknown, the council guard serve the most elite members of ratfolk society with an unquestioning loyalty almost alien to most ratfolk. No amount of bribery or coercion can shake a guard member's loyalty. They are even mute, thus preventing them from accidentally spilling any of their master's secrets. 


<br>

In combat, these hulking warriors fight with many times the ferocity of an ordinary war vermin. Their implacable natures mean they will fight to the death if necessary, and no amount of magic can charm or frighten them into submission. 

#### Art Credit 
* Nezumi Bladeblesser - Ilse Gort, Wizards of the Coast
* Watery Grave - Raymond Swanland, Wizards of the Coast

### Ratfolk Warlords

Though ratfolk aren’t known for their valor or powers of leadership, those that rise to the top of their martial <br> hierarchy possess an underhanded ferocity that can’t <br> be denied. These warlords combine martial skill, <br> devious tactics, and the ability to rally their otherwise <br> cowardly kin, making them foes that are <br> underestimated all too often. Even when a ratfolk <br> force appears to be routing, one rallying cry from <br> their warlord can turn them from a fleeing army <br> to one that’s quickly overwhelming their <br> overconfident enemies. 

When engaging enemies, ratfolk warlords can <br> utilize an array of weaponry, though brutal <br> spike fists are among their most favored tools. <br> They never fight fair and often use feinting <br> tactics, fleeing from  enemies who appear to <br> have a strong position and striking back at <br> them the moment they show weakness. <br> These strategies also serve to distract and <br> draw out their foes, allowing their minions to <br> surround and swarm the now vulnerable targets.

#### Art Credit
* Marrow-Gnawer - Wayne Reynolds, <Br>Wizards of the Coast

### Ratfolk Soldiers & Seers Tactics
Most of these ratfolk use the standard tactics described in the Running Ratfolk Adventures section (pg. 4). The differences between different types of soldiers mostly come down to how disciplined they are, with the weaker ratfolk being the least reliable and the more powerful ratfolk being more stalwart and better able to coordinate and execute their tactics. 

The presence of a ratfolk leader makes a big difference in how long a ratfolk force will hold out before routing, and someone as powerful as a warlord or grey prophet can keep the minions in their immediate vicinity in the fight far longer than they would otherwise hold out before fleeing. 

The following ratfolk have some unique considerations to keep in mind.

#### Tactics: Ratfolk Slaves
These wretches are generally used as cannon fodder by other ratfolk. They often spend as much time fleeing the players as they do fighting them. This “strategy” does give them a better shot at using their Cornered Rat ability before they are slain. Ratfolk slaves are also considered so expendable by other ratfolk that seeing them fleeing or slain isn’t a bother, and other ratfolk are unlikely to break and flee as a result.

#### Tactics: Council Guards
These are the most elite ratfolk soldiers and most atypical of their kind in terms of their combat behavior. Their primary goal is to safeguard their commander, and their Scurry Towards feature lets them intercept players trying to chase down said commander. Council guards will also never flee a fight if doing so would put the commander in jeopardy.

#### Tactics: Grey Prophet
Like most spellcasters, grey prophets will try to stay out of reach of the players and use minions as a meat shield. *Fissure* is an excellent spell for creating terrain that impedes the players, and Vermintide can be used to drop tides of rats on players who’ve fallen into the fissure or are trying to attack the grey prophet. If players do manage to close into melee range, the hex staff attacks do high damage and prevent reactions, giving the grey prophet an opening to retreat.

\columnbreak

### Ratfolk Soldiers & Seers Loot
Because ratfolk are humanoids, most of the valuable goods that can be looted from them are the remains of the equipment they were using or valuables they were carrying or hiding nearby. Most of the challenge of looting ratfolk is identifying which materials they're carrying that have functional value.

Finding valuables can be done using an **Intelligence (Investigation)** or **Wisdom (Perception)** check, depending on the circumstance. In the case of a grey prophet, you may use an **Intelligence (Arcana)** or **Intelligence (Religion)** check instead. 


#### Ratfolk Soldiers & Seers Loot Tables
The following tables describe the number of items and value of those items the players are able to loot depending on the result of their check or the results of your roll. If they're making checks, you can have them make a separate check for each creature they're looting or use one check for multiple creatures at once to save time.

|:---:|:-----------:|
|  1-5  | Nothing |
|  6-11 | 1 5sp Item | 
|  12-16 | 1d4(2) 5sp Items |  
|  17-20 | 1d6(3) 5sp Items |  
|  21+ | 1d4(2) 1gp Items |  

##### Ratfolk Warrior Loot Table

## Ratfolk Eldritch Engineers

The eldritch engineers are a horrifying fusion of sorcerer, scientist, and engineer, embodying the raw ambition and unbounded deviousness of the ratfolk. They are selected from the most cunning and intelligent of their brood, demonstrating exceptional skill and a ruthless ingenuity to rise above their kin.

Their role is dual-natured, as they devote equal time to the study of arcane arts and the sciences of engineering and alchemy. Their lairs are often cluttered with both arcane artifacts and complex mechanical devices. They use their knowledge to forge devastating weapons, animate mad vehicles, and manipulate the very fabric of reality.

A eldritch engineer is a terrifying sight to behold, a grim fusion of organic and mechanical. Their hunched bodies, wrapped in shadowy robes, are an intricate network of self-made, mechanical augmentations and arcane devices, often lit by the eerie glow of the irradiated minerals they utilize.


\columnbreak


<br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br>

They stand slightly taller than the average ratfolk, though their hunched posture can sometimes belie their true height. Their fur is usually patchy and discolored from constant exposure to their potent power source, and their eyes gleam with an unsettling, predatory intelligence.

Body parts lost in combat or laboratory mishaps are commonly replaced with mechanical augmentations. These range from simple, metallic prosthetics to complex contraptions designed to enhance physical capabilities. An eldritch engineer might have a multi-jointed mechanical arm equipped with various tools and weaponry, or a prosthetic leg with incorporated shock-absorbing springs for enhanced agility.

Their heads are often adorned with complex eyepieces that serve as telescopes, microscopes, or even as targeting systems for their weapons. They might have a network of tubes and wires injected into their bodies, delivering a constant supply of the irradiated minerals to boost their magical prowess and physical resilience.



<img src='https://i.ibb.co/5kYkZ43/Nashi-Moon-Sages-Scion-Kamigawa-Neon-Dynasty-Mt-G-Art.jpg' style='position:absolute; top:-0px; right:-180px; width:1100px;' />

<img src='https://www.gmbinder.com/images/WGybwnz.png' style='position:absolute; top:345px; right:103px; width:950px; filter:  grayscale(00%) brightness(97%); transform:rotate(25deg)' />


<img src='https://www.gmbinder.com/images/WGybwnz.png' style='position:absolute; top:370px; right:-250px; width:900px; filter:  grayscale(00%) brightness(97%); transform:rotate(0deg)' />



\pagebreakNum

The eldritch engineers are known for their intricate and devastating arsenal, a testament to their wicked blend of magic and technology. Their weapons, powered by the potent, irradiated minerals they mine from the depths, are as diverse as they are deadly.

Eldritch engineers have innovated a line of firearms that stand apart from any standard weaponry. These include eldritch muskets and pistols whose barrels are etched with arcane runes and loaded with shards of the irradiated mineral, not mere lead shot. When fired, these weapons unleash blasts of magical energy that can tear through armor and sear flesh, leaving behind wounds that fester with otherworldly radiation.

Beyond these "standard" weapons, each engineer builds their own custom devious devices to bring into battle and test on unwitting foes. These machines range from flamethrowers to rocket launchers to machines capable of generating seismic tremors. This makes every encounter with a eldritch engineer a wildly unpredictable affair, as there's no predicting what the mad rat will whip out next.

To power these devious devices, eldritch engineers can channel eldritch power through their partially mechanical forms, building up higher and higher levels over time. Once their bodies are crackling with power, they will channel it all through one of their deadly weapons, unleashing a wave of devastation upon as many foes as possible. If a few minions become collateral damage in the process, then so be it. It's a small price to pay for a successful weapons test.

___
___

This movement doesn't provoke opportunity attacks. While frightened this way, the ratfolk can only take the Dash, Disengage, Dodge, or Hide action. This feature ignores immunity to the frightened condition.

### Master Eldritch Engineer

The master eldritch engineers are the epitome of the ratfolk's insidious ambition and genius, representing the pinnacle of their society's arcane-technological mastery. They are the eldritch engineers' most accomplished, the most advanced, and the maddest of the mad, possessing the deadliest inventions and the power to command and control their brethren. Their status is not given lightly; each master eldritch engineer must prove their worth through arcane prowess, engineering genius, and a ruthless drive for power. 


Master eldritch engineer are often more machine than flesh, with a plethora of mechanical limbs, arcane enhancements, and complex devices incorporated into their being. Their enhancements are the most sophisticated, often made from rare and highly durable materials, imbued with powerful spells for protection and strength. Some even replace their hearts with mechanical pumps powered by irradiated minerals, extending their lifespan and imbuing them with incredible resilience.

A master eldritch engineer's workshop is a sprawling labyrinth of machinery and magic, stretching across massive underground halls. Here, amidst the controlled chaos of their laboratories, they construct their masterpieces of destruction. The air buzzes with raw arcane power, while countless mechanical constructs work tirelessly to bring their master's visions to life.

As the leaders of their society, master eldritch engineers hold the highest authority, guiding the actions of their underlings with an iron fist. Their word is law in the warren, and their orders are executed without question. However, their authority is not entirely unchallenged, as each master eldritch engineer is a potential rival, leading to a complex web of alliances, betrayals, and power struggles.

Above all, master eldritch engineers are visionaries in their own twisted way. They harbor grand dreams of surfacing from their subterranean confines to dominate the world above. And through their ever-evolving schemes and growing arsenal of minions and mad machinery, they are always moving closer to making their dreams a reality.
___
___

### The Ratfolk Chief <br> Eldritch Engineer
This enigmatic figure stands as a testament to the melding of arcane mastery and mechanical ingenuity, a force that has irrevocably altered the course of his kind's evolution. Driven by a relentless desire to harness destructive power, The Chief Eldritch Engineer has transcended his ratfolk origins to become a fearsome harbinger of technological annihilation.

The Chief Eldritch Engineer is a figure more imposing than the typical ratfolk, standing tall and hunched, his silhouette commanding both respect and trepidation. He carries the marks of his relentless pursuit of power, with a body mutilated by weapons and experiments gone awry. His form is a blend of living flesh and cold machinery, for he has replaced missing and damaged body parts with a symphony of mechanical devices. Most notable is his mechanical clawed arm, an emblem of his relentless drive for dominance over both arcane and mechanical forces. Upon his back, he bears whirring devices that are forever channeling eldritch power, a testament to his mastery of the arcane arts.

Armed with the fearsome halberd known as Storm Demon, The Chief Eldritch Engineer commands the very elements to his will. With a single swing, this weapon can discharge blasts of lightning, leaving destruction in its wake. His arsenal is further augmented by an array of terrible devices, each capable of unleashing devastation upon his enemies. Whether shooting torrents of fire or lightning, launching rockets that scream through the air, deploying poison gas clouds that choke his foes, or even tearing holes in the fabric of reality itself, his arsenal knows no bounds. He possesses an uncanny ability to enhance these devices beyond the capabilities of a typical eldritch engineer.

\columnbreak

<br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br>

 In dire circumstances, he might pilot a vermin wheel, or strategically deploy Power Conduits before a battle to replenish his arcane energy, ensuring a relentless onslaught.

The Chief Eldritch Engineer is no mere recluse; his insatiable thirst for knowledge and power has driven him to traverse the world, stealing magical and technological secrets from other races and civilizations. Through relentless espionage, manipulation, and even ruthless confrontations, he has accumulated a repository of forbidden knowledge. His interactions with other cultures have allowed him to adapt foreign technology to his twisted vision, further fueling his deadly arsenal.

Renowned for his profound contribution to ratfolk society, The Chief Eldritch Engineer stands as the inventor of many of their most potent weapons. His relentless pursuit of innovation has granted the ratfolk technological advancements that would have been inconceivable without his genius. Thus, his reputation as a visionary in the realm of technological annihilation is cemented, earning him the prestigious title of Chief Eldritch Engineer.

Beneath his imposing visage lies a mind consumed by a singular obsession: the creation of the most destructive weapons imaginable. The Chief Eldritch Engineer is driven not by allegiance to a cause, but by a relentless desire to prove his ability to bring the world to ruin. Neither loyalty to his own kind nor concern for collateral damage can deter him from his path. He views the world through a lens of devastation, where every creation, every experiment, only deepens his resolve to surpass his previous achievements, even if it means bringing his own kind to the brink of extinction.

> ### Legendary Actions
> The ratfolk can take 3 legendary actions, choosing from the options below. Only one legendary action option can be used at a time and only at the end of another creature's turn. The ratfolk regains spent legendary actions at the start of its turn.
> 
> **Check.** The ratfolk makes a skill check that would normally require an action.
>
> **Move.**  The ratfolk or vehicle it is piloting moves up to 20 feet without provoking opportunity attacks. It can use this legendary action while frightened by its Scurry Away feature.
>
> **Tenacious Will.** If the ratfolk is suffering from an effect that allows it to make a saving throw as an action or at the beginning or end of its next turn, it may immediately make that save against the effect with advantage. It can use this legendary action while incapacitated and while frightened by its Scurry Away feature.
>



\pagebreakNum

> ##### Alternate Weapon: Hexmusket
>You can replace the Eldritch Pistol and Hex Blade of any eldritch engineer or master eldritch engineer with a Hexmusket, which it can use with the following action.
>
> **Hexmusket.** *Ranged Weapon Attack:* +6 to hit, (range 150/450), one target. *Hit:* 12 (2d8 + 3) piercing damage plus 7 (2d6) radiant damage. If the ratfolk rolls a 3 or lower on the attack roll, the attack automatically misses as the musket malfunctions and the ratfolk takes the attack damage. A fired musket must be reloaded using an action before it can be fired again. 
>
> If an eldritch master is using the weapon, it instead gets +9 to hit and deals 14 (2d8 + 5) piercing damage plus 7 (2d6) radiant damage on hit.

<br>

> ##### Piloting Vehicles
> If you're using vehicles in your games and want your ratfolk engineers to be masters of piloting them, you can add
> the following attribute to eldritch engineers and master eldritch engineers:
>
> ***Devious Driver.*** The ratfolk can pilot vehicles as a bonus action even while frightened by its Scurry Away feature (this doesn't allow the vehicle to be piloted multiple times in a round).
>
> Additionally, when the ratfolk uses its Scurry Away feature, it can have a vehicle it's piloting move up to 15 feet away rather than flee on foot.
>
> Finally, when the ratfolk pilots a vehicle, it can expend any number of eldritch power levels to increase the speed of the vehicle by 10 feet per power level expended until the end of the turn.

\columnbreak

### Epic Chief Eldritch Engineer Battle

If you wish to make the chief eldritch into an endgame threat, you can have him start the encounter piloting a **wheelz of doom** crewed with an **irradiated rat tide** and give him the following trait; this increases the CR of the encounter to CR 23: <br>


***Devious Master Driver.*** The ratfolk can pilot vehicles even while affected by its Scurry Away feature (this doesn't allow the vehicle to be piloted multiple times in a round). When the ratfolk uses its Scurry Away feature, it can have the vehicle it's piloting move up to 15 feet away rather than flee on foot.

Additionally, when the ratfolk pilots a vehicle, it can expend any number of eldritch power levels to increase the speed of the vehicle by 10 feet per power level expended until the end of the turn.

Finally, the ratfolk can't be moved or teleported from a vehicle it's piloting against its will, and when the ratfolk would take damage, it can choose to have the vehicle take the damage instead.

### Power Conduits
If the chief eldritch engineer is fighting in his lair, you can increase the challenge of the encounter by giving him access to power conduits built to charge his powers. Each power conduit is a large magical object with 60 hit points, resistance to all damage, and an AC of 19. You can place one or more of these power conduits throughout the lair, and each power conduit added increases the chief eldritch engineer's Challenge Rating by 1.

At the end of the chief engineer's turn, he can choose to start drawing power from the nearest conduit, creating a beam between him and the conduit; the chief engineer can do this even if he is incapacitated. While the beam is active, the conduit loses all resistances. The beam will break if the chief engineer moves more than 100 feet away from it, if he has total cover from the conduit, or if either the chief engineer or the conduit is reduced to 0 hit points. Any creature or object that moves through the beam can also break it, but it takes 22 (5d8) lightning damage as a result.

If the chief engineer starts his next turn with the beam still intact, the beam dissipates, and he may choose to either roll an additional 2d4 when activating his Unlimited Power trait this turn or end a spell of 4th level or lower in his lair.







<img src='https://i.ibb.co/Ttx3xZB/Reckoner-Bankbuster-Kamigawa-Neon-Dynasty-Mt-G-Art.jpg' style='position:absolute; bottom:-130px; right:220px; width:750px; transform: scaleX(1)' />

 <img src='https://www.gmbinder.com/images/cPPYV7h.png' 
  style='position:absolute;right:-636px;top:0px;height:1400px;width:1416px;transform:rotate(65deg)' />

\pagebreakNum

### Forbidden Devices

Ratfolk eldritch engineers possess a unique arsenal of magic items specifically designed for use against their adversaries. An eldritch engineer can select two items, while a master eldritch engineer can select three from the list below. The chief eldritch engineer can select 4 devices from the list below and gains an extra damage type resistance along with a new legendary action as part of his Forbidden Enhancements feature. 

The same device can be chosen more than once. Each device requires an action to use and can't be used again until the engineer has had time to rebuild it using Smith's Tools during a long rest.


#### Brass Orb
This fist-sized metal orb made of interlocking whirling cogs is  capable of causing a momentary tear in reality.

If the ratfolk is not restrained or grappled, it can throw the device at a point it can see within 30 feet. The brass orb detonates at this point, and each creature within 15 feet of it that’s not behind total cover must make a Dexterity saving throw, taking 13 (3d8) force damage plus an additional 4 (1d8) force damage for each eldritch energy level the ratfolk expended on a failed save, or half as much damage on a successful one. If this damage reduces a target to 20 hit points or fewer and it failed the saving throw, it is banished to another plane of existence of the DM's choice.

When the ratfolk attempts to throw the brass orb, creatures can use their reaction to make opportunity attacks against it as though it moved out of their reach. If a creature hits the ratfolk this way, it drops the brass orb, which detonates at its location.



##### Brass Orb: Forbidden Enhancement
**Damage Type Resistance:** Force<br>
**New Legendary Action:** A target creature within 120 feet of the ratfolk that the ratfolk can see must make a DC 19 Charisma saving throw. On a failed save, the target is teleported to an unoccupied space of the ratfolk's choice that it can see within 20 feet of the target. The chosen space must be on a surface or in a liquid that can support the target without the target having to squeeze.

#### Doom Rocket
When launched, this missile shrieks through the air before striking the ground and unleashing a wave of bright, glowing green light that irradiates anything near the impact site.

The ratfolk cannot use this device if it is restrained or grappled. When the ratfolk uses the Doom Rocket, it expends all its eldritch energy levels and launches it at a point it can see within 120 feet. The rocket detonates at this point, and each creature within 30 feet of it must make a Constitution saving throw, taking 16 (3d10) radiant damage plus an additional 5 (1d10) radiant damage for each eldritch energy level the ratfolk expended on a failed save, or half as much damage on a successful one.

When the ratfolk attempts to launch the rocket, <Br> creatures can use their reaction to make opportunity <br> attacks against it. If a creature hits the ratfolk in this way, <br> the rocket misfires and detonates at its location.

\columnbreak

##### Doom Rocket: Forbidden Enhancement
**Damage Type Resistance:** Radiant<br>
**New Legendary Action:** The ratfolk makes a Ranged or Melee Spell Attack, with a +11 to hit, a reach of 5 feet, or a range of 100/400 feet, targeting one creature. On a hit, the target takes 9 (2d8) radiant damage, and if the target is a creature, it becomes irradiated for the next minute. At the end of the irradiated creature's turn, it must make a DC 19 Constitution saving throw. On a failed save, both it and each creature within 10 feet of it take 9 (2d8) radiant damage; on a successful save, the irradiated effect ends. A *lesser restoration spell* will remove the radiation.

#### Earth Render

This mechanized spike jackhammers into the ground, creating a localized earthquake capable of reducing the structures of surface dwellers into rubble.

When the ratfolk uses the Earth Render, it expends all its eldritch energy levels and rams the device into the ground, creating violent tremors. Each creature in a 25-foot cube originating from the ratfolk must succeed on a Dexterity saving throw or take 10 (3d6) bludgeoning damage plus an additional 3 (1d6) for each energy level the ratfolk expended and be knocked prone. A creature that succeeds on its saving throw takes half as much damage and isn’t knocked prone. Structures in the area take double damage from the effect.

##### Earth Render: Forbidden Enhancement
**Damage Type Resistance:** Thunder<br>
**New Legendary Action:** A creature of the ratfolk's choice standing on earth or stone within 60 feet of the ratfolk must make a DC 19 Strength saving throw or be buried as it sinks into the ground. A buried creature becomes restrained. Any creature, including the buried creature, can use its action to free the buried creature by succeeding on a DC 19 Strength check. If the creature attempting the rescue has a burrow speed, it has advantage on this check.

#### Hex Lightning Generator
This strange metallic device hums with power before emitting a tremendous bolt of green lightning.

When the ratfolk uses the Hex Lightning Generator, it expends all its eldritch energy levels and hurls a magical green lightning bolt at a point it can see within 100 feet. Each creature within 10 feet of that point must succeed on a Dexterity saving throw or take 13 (3d8) lightning damage plus an additional 4 (1d8) for each eldritch energy level the ratfolk expended and become unable to take reactions until the start of its next turn. A creature that succeeds on its saving throw takes half as much damage and doesn't lose its reaction.
 
##### Hex Lighting Generator: Forbidden Enhancement
**Damage Type Resistance:** Lightning<br>
**New Legendary Action:** The ratfolk makes a Ranged or Melee Spell Attack, with a +11 to hit, a reach of 5 feet, or a range of 100/400 feet, targeting one creature. On a hit, the target takes 9 (2d8) lightning damage, and if the target is a creature, it becomes charged with hex electricity. At the end of the charged creature's next turn, the electricity deals 18 (4d8) lightning damage, after which the hex electricity dissipates. Another creature that touches the charged creature can choose to take the lightning damage immediately, thereby ending the effect.
  

 
#### Hex Fume Sprayer
This device's canister contains toxic gases that can be expelled in a wave through a large, rusty nozzle. 

When the ratfolk uses the Hex Fume Sprayer, it expends all its eldritch energy levels and sprays toxic fumes in a 30-foot cone. Each creature in that area must succeed on a Constitution saving throw or take 9 (2d8) poison damage plus an additional 5 (1d8) poison damage for each eldritch energy level the ratfolk expended and become poisoned until the start of the ratfolk's next turn. A creature that succeeds on its saving throw takes half as much damage and isn't poisoned.
 
\columnbreak

##### Hex Fume Sprayer: Forbidden Enhancement
**Damage Type Resistance:** Poison<br>
**New Legendary Action:** The ratfolk releases a cloud of poison gas in a 5-foot radius sphere at a point within 60 feet of itself, heavily obscuring the area. The cloud lasts for one minute or until a wind of moderate or greater speed (at least 10 miles per hour) disperses it.

When a creature enters an area covered by one or more of these gas clouds for the first time on a turn or starts its turn in one or more gas clouds, that creature must make a DC 19 Constitution saving throw. On a failed save, the creature takes 13 (3d8) poison damage and is poisoned until the end of its next turn. On a successful save, the creature takes half as much damage and isn't poisoned.

#### Hex Scorcher
This arm-mounted flamethrower spews lines of flames that cling to anything in their path.

When the ratfolk uses the Hex Scorcher, it expends all its eldritch energy levels to unleash a gout of flame 30 feet long and 5 feet wide in the direction of its choice. Each creature in that area must succeed on a Dexterity saving throw or take 13 (3d8) fire damage plus an additional 4 (1d8) for each energy level the ratfolk expended and be set on fire. A creature that succeeds on its saving throw takes half as much damage and isn't set on fire. A creature that's been set on fire this way takes 9 (2d8) fire damage at the end of each of its turns until a creature uses an action to douse the fire.



##### Hex Scorcher: Forbidden Enhancement
**Damage Type Resistance:** Fire<br>
**New Legendary Action:** The ratfolk makes a Ranged or Melee Spell Attack, with a +11 to hit, a reach of 5 feet, or a range of 100/400 feet, targeting one creature. On a hit, the target takes 9 (2d8) fire damage, and if the target is a creature, it is set on fire. Until a creature uses an action to douse the fire, the burning creature takes 9 (2d8) fire damage at the end of each of its turns.

##### Eldritch Engineer Adventure Hooks

| d12  | Plot Hook |
|:---:|:-----------:|
|  1  | **The Lost Contraption:** The players find a strange device with an unknown function. Little do they know it's the lost invention of a eldritch engineer who seeks to recover it to complete his devious plans. The players seek to destroy the device or attempt to determine its function so they can better understand the warlock's schemes and how to stop them.|
|  2  |**Underground Espionage:** A mysterious informant suggests that a master eldritch engineer is plotting a massive assault on a surface city. The adventurers must infiltrate the labyrinthine warrens, gather intelligence about the potential attack, and sabotage it if possible.|
|  3 | **Unstable Alliance:** A master eldritch engineer, embroiled in a power struggle with his rivals, offers a temporary alliance with the surface dwellers. He promises to share crucial information about the other master eldritch engineers' plans in exchange for the party's help in securing his position.|
|  4  |**Raid the Workshop:** A series of unusual seismic activities has been traced back to eldritch engineers' workshops. The party is tasked to raid the workshop, neutralize the source of the tremors, and escape before they're overrun by ratfolk and their inventions.|
|  5  |**Race for the Power Source:** An enormous vein of the irradiated mineral has been discovered. The party and the ratfolk learn about it at the same time, leading to a race to secure control of the mineral, lest it become a weapon in the hands of the eldritch engineers.|
|  6  | **The Stolen River:** A key river has inexplicably dried up, leading to potential famines. The party discovers that an eldritch engineer is diverting the river underground for some nefarious purpose, threatening both surface and underground ecosystems.|
|  7  |**The Mad Master’s Doomsday Device:** A master eldritch engineer has constructed a doomsday device that threatens to engulf the entire region in an arcane explosion. The adventurers must find a way to disarm the device and confront the master eldritch engineer in his heavily guarded stronghold.|



\columnbreak

<br><br>

|   |  |
|:---:|:-----------:|
|  8  | **The Defector:** An eldritch engineer seeks to defect to the surface, bringing with him valuable knowledge about the workings of ratfolk technology. The party must protect the defector from vengeful kin while ensuring he's not a double agent planted by a cunning master eldritch engineer.|
|  9  | **The Doomsday Device:** The Chief Eldritch engineer unveils a colossal doomsday device, capable of reshaping the very fabric of reality. The players are tasked with infiltrating the eldritch engineer's heavily fortified lair to dismantle the device. Along the way, they encounter traps, minions, and devious defenses designed to protect the engineer's magnum opus. |
|  10  |**Stolen Arcana:** The Chief Eldritch Engineer's insatiable thirst for knowledge has led him to abduct renowned spellcasters from various corners of the world. The players are approached by a desperate mage whose mentor has gone missing. As they uncover the truth, they realize that the eldritch engineer seeks to extract arcane secrets to enhance his weapons of destruction. |
|  11 | **Arcano-Tech Black Market:** Reports of strange and devastating weapons emerging on the black market draw the players' attention. Investigating the source leads them to a hidden marketplace where The Chief Eldritch Engineer secretly trades his forbidden creations. The adventurers must infiltrate the black market, gather evidence of his activities, and dismantle the network before the eldritch engineer's weapons fall into the wrong hands.|
|  12  |**The Rival Warlock:** A rival warlock, equally obsessed with power, challenges The Chief Eldritch Engineer's reign as the master of destruction. The adventurers become entangled in a power struggle between these two malevolent forces, and they must decide whether to aid one eldritch over the other or seek to dismantle both before their feud spirals out of control.|

### Eldritch Engineer Tactics
Eldritch engineers, along with master engineers, are extremely intelligent ratfolk who delight in testing their diabolical weaponry on players. In combat, their primary objective is to eliminate as many targets as possible using their advanced artillery, often disregarding the casualties of their own minions caught in the crossfire.

Eldritch engineers possess a versatile arsenal, including ranged attacks, area of effect damage, and some melee capabilities. When using a vehicle, they can also serve as cavalry units, making their tactical approach highly adaptable. Their power output each turn depends on their eldritch power level.

**Initiation.** At the start of combat, the engineer will attempt to fire its pistol, reload as a bonus action, and fire again, maximizing damage against a target surrounded by minions.

**Closing In.** The eldritch engineer can also utilize its hex blade, which consumes eldritch power levels for amplified damage. When opting for this strategy, the eldritch engineer will usually first shoot with the pistol, then engage in melee combat with the hex blade. This attack option is best used when an enemy is lower on health or when the ratfolk and its allies greatly outnumber their opponents.

**Hexmuskets.** If equipped with a musket, the engineer maintains a greater distance from enemies while firing at surrounded foes to use its Overwhelming Mass feature.

#### Forbidden Devices

When deciding whether to use Forbidden Devices, the engineer considers the available eldritch power levels and the number of potential targets. A handy trick when trying to decide if the engineer will use a device on any given turn is to consider each power level it has and the number of targets it could hit as individual incentives. At the start of its turn, if there are 4 or more "incentives," it will likely use the device.

\columnbreak

The engineer does not hesitate to sacrifice its own minions when using its devices unless the minions hold significant value. Lesser ratfolk soldiers are generally considered disposable.



#### Retreat 
Warlocks retreat from combat when they're outnumbered two to one in melee, their health drops below one-third, or they run out of Forbidden Devices or minions. During a retreat, they can still reload their weapon, enabling the engineer with a musket to keep its distance from melee opponents while taking pot shots at their pursuers.

#### Serving As Repair Rats
With their high-level tools skills and ability to perform tool checks even while frightened by their Scurry Away feature, eldritch engineers can act as mobile repair rats, helping sustain weapons teams or vehicles. They cease repairs only when there is nothing left to fix or when deploying a Forbidden Device presents a greater incentive.

For an eldritch engineer serving as a backline repair rat, equipping them with doom rockets, a hex lightning generator, and a musket is recommended, as this allows them to function as true artillery masters.

#### Mounted on Vehicles

Eldritch engineers with vehicles stick to ranged attacks combined with opportunistic hit-and-run strikes. They assault the enemy with Forbidden Devices and gunfire, then charge when they identify a weakness or accumulate a significant number of eldritch power levels for a high-damage vehicle crash. The thrill of crushing an enemy with a lightning-fast vehicle often entices engineers to charge in, even when it may not be the most strategic choice. An engineer armed with a hex blade and hexlock pistol is more inclined to engage in melee combat compared to one equipped with a musket.

<img src='https://i.ibb.co/SrHFjj5/nezumi-freewheeler.png' style='position:absolute; bottom:-130px; right:-3px; width:823px; transform: scaleX(1)' />

 <img src='https://www.gmbinder.com/images/cPPYV7h.png' 
  style='position:absolute;right:-10px;top:-430px;height:1400px;width:1416px;transform:rotate(-0deg)' />

\pagebreakNum


### Chief Eldritch Engineer Tactics

The chief engineer is a cunning rat with an intense desire to obliterate foes with his impressive array of technological prowess. The strategies outlined below are designed to optimize his capabilities while offering clear cues to opponents, allowing them to form counter strategies so they gain a sense of agency in combat.

#### Unlimited Power!
This ability turns the battle into a race against time. The chief eldritch engineer will either overpower his adversaries with immense damage or succumb to his own power surges.


#### Forbidden Devices
The chief engineer possesses four Forbidden Devices, and he is quick to employ them when faced with significant threats. If he has three or more eldritch power levels, he will activate a device every turn. Alternatively, he'll use them whenever he can target three or more enemies. However, he will always keep one device in reserve to grant him an extra Legendary Action thanks to his Forbidden Augmentation ability.

When the engineer uses a device selected for his Forbidden Augmentation as a legendary action, he will usually activate the same device as an action on his subsequent turn. This sequence provides players with both a warning of what the device can do and an escalating sense of drama leading up to the device's deployment. 

**Brass Orb & Earth Render.** These legendary actions should be used to manipulate enemy positioning to maximize their impact when they're used as actions.


**Hex Scorcher & Hex Lightning Generator.** These legendary actions can be used to bait opponents into aiding their allies, tricking them into grouping together so they can all be hit by the device's actions.

**Doom Rocket & Hex Fume Sprayer.** These legendary actions  can be used to make parts of the battlefield hazardous for players, thus herding them into positions where the device's action can be used to best effect.

#### Legendary Actions and Scurry Away
The engineer uses standard legendary actions when he needs to make an escape or when his capabilities are being hindered. Should he remain in jeopardy after using all his legendary actions, he will use Scurry Away as a last resort.


#### Epic Chief Eldritch Engineer Battle

In this encounter, the engineer's tactics align with those detailed for vermin wheels. A notable advantage he has in vehicle such as the vermin wheel is that his Move legendary action allows him to ram targets with the wheel. If he can't reach a target this way, he'll rely on his Forbidden Augmentation legendary actions. 

While operating the vermin wheel, the engineer refrains from deploying any Forbidden Devices as actions. Instead, he channels all his eldritch power into the vehicle, biding his time until he's amassed sufficient power.

#### Power Conduits 
While a battle with these items present doesn't drastically alter the engineer's tactics, it does make him prioritize targets attempting to attack the conduits he's channeling.

<img src='https://i.ibb.co/N9p1gJx/Beacon-Bolt-Guilds-of-Ravnica-Mt-G-Art.jpg' style='position:absolute; bottom:-40px; right:-700px; width:1495px; transform:scaleX(-1);filter:opacity(100%);'/>

### Eldritch Engineer Loot
Because ratfolk are humanoids, most of the valuable goods that can be looted from them are the remains of the equipment they were using or valuables they were carrying or hiding nearby. Most of the challenge of looting ratfolk engineers is identifying what devices they're carrying still have any functional value.

In the case of the chief eldritch engineer, not only will he have the highest quality items for looting, but he will likely have magic items and other valuables that can be part of a treasure hoard, including its magic weapon, *storm demon*.

Finding valuables can be done using an **Intelligence (Investigation)** or **Wisdom (Perception)** check, depending on the circumstance. If the identifying value materials the ratfolk was carrying will likely require an **Intelligence (Arcana)** check or a check using proficiency with appropriate tools, such as Smith's Tools, Tinker's Tools, or Alchemist's Supplies.


#### Eldritch Engineer Loot Tables
The following tables describe the number of items and value of those items the players are able to loot depending on the result of their check or the results of your roll. If they're making checks, you can have them make a separate check for each creature they're looting or use one check for multiple creatures at once to save time.

|  8-10 | 1d4(2) 5gp Items |

|  17-22 | 1d4(2) 20gp Items  |  
|  23+ |  1d6(3) 20gp Items |

## Ratfolk Weapons Operators

In the deep and twisted labyrinths of the underworld, where survival is a test of cunning and ambition, the ratfolk have harnessed deadly innovations in a bid to claim power. Among their ranks, a special caste stands out - the Weapon Operators. These ratfolk are not merely the handlers of their lethal creations, but ambitious individuals eager to rise through the societal ranks, driven by the intoxicating allure of power these weapons offer.

The Weapon Operators are chosen for their cunning and strength, but their selection is just as much a product of their own ruthless ambition. They yearn for the power the weapons represent, covet the respect and fear they command in their kin's eyes, and aspire to the elevated status these roles bring within their clan.

Operating the ratfolk's terrifying arsenal is a display of dominance and superiority, a tangible sign of their high-ranking position. Each use of their weapon reinforces their status, reminding all around them of the raw power they control. It is a potent mix of fear and respect, a heady cocktail that fuels their ambition and desire to rise even higher.

However, the confidence these weapons bring only lasts so long as the battle is going in their favor. Ratfolk weapon operators are quick to abandon their weapons to save their own skins.  Those ratfolk who stick with their weapon while frightened and on the backfoot are more likely to make panicked and desperate decisions with their weapon.



\columnbreak

<br><br><br><br><br>

 This ironically puts them in more danger as they increase the risk of a devastating mishap. Conversely, if the ratfolk feel they have their enemy on the backfoot and victory is at hand, they may also engage in reckless use of their weapon as they become overconfident, leading them to snatch defeat from the jaws of victory as they cause an untimely mishap.

As such, the path of the Weapon Operator is perilous, laden with risks as volatile as the weapons they wield. Many ambitious ratfolk, lured by the promise of power, meet an untimely end, falling victim to the very weapons they hoped would be their salvation. The weapons do not discriminate between friend and foe; a minor miscalculation or a moment's inattention can lead to a catastrophic explosion, reducing the ambitious ratfolk to a cautionary tale.

Ratfolk who survive long enough eventually become veteran weapon operators. Having endured countless battles and weapon malfunctions, these ratfolk have developed faster reflexed and become substantially tougher than their less experienced kin. They have a more intuitive understanding of how to push the limits of their weapon and maximize its destructive potential while limiting the risks to themselves. However, despite their veteran status, these ratfolk still carry the same tendencies as the rest of their kin and utilize the same underhanded and often cowardly tactics.

<br>


___

> ## Ratfolk Weapon Operator
>*Medium humanoid (ratfolk), chaotic evil*
> ___
> - **Armor Class** 13 (hazmat suit)
> - **Hit Points** 22 (4d8 + 4)
> - **Speed** 30 ft.
>___
>|STR|DEX|CON|INT|WIS|CHA|
>|:---:|:---:|:---:|:---:|:---:|:---:|
>|10 (0)|14 (+2)|12 (+1)|10 (+0)|10 (0)|8 (-1)|
>___
> - **Skills** Acrobatics +4, Deception +1, Stealth +4, Land Vehicles +2, Leatherworker's Tools +2, Tinker's Tools +4
> - **Damage Resistances** One damage type other then bludgeoning, piercing, or slashing (It can change the damage type after a long rest if it has Leatherworker's Tools on hand.)
> - **Senses** darkvision 60 ft., passive Perception 10
> - **Languages** Common, Undercommon
> - **Challenge** 1/4 (50 XP) &emsp;&emsp;&emsp;&emsp;    **Proficiency Bonus** +2
> ___
>
> ***Abandon Post.*** When The ratfolk uses its Scurry Away feature it, it may leave a two-creature weapon it is part of or exit a vehicle without spending any movement, using actions and without provoking attacks of opportunity.
>
> ***Crevice Crawler.*** The ratfolk can move through and stop in a space large enough to fit a creature one size smaller than it without squeezing.
>
> ***Keen Smell.*** The ratfolk has advantage on Wisdom (Perception) checks that rely on smell.
>
> ***Overwhelming Mass x1.*** The first time each turn that the ratfolk hits a creature with an attack, it deals an extra 1 damage per ally it has within 5 feet of its target that isn't incapacitated. The ratfolk can benefit from up to 3 allies this way.
>
> ***Panicked Job.*** The ratfolk may make repair checks on and activate any of the functions of two-creature weapons and siege weapons while frightened by its Scurry Away feature. If it activates any of the functions of a two-creature weapon while frightened this way, the next time the weapon rolls to check for a mishap, it rolls an additional dice.
>
> ### Actions
>
> ***Club.*** *Melee Weapon Attack:* +4 to hit, reach 5 ft., one creature. *Hit:* 4 (1d4 + 2) bludgeoning damage.
>
> ### Reactions
>
> ***Scurry Away.***  When an enemy the ratfolk can see ends its turn, the ratfolk can move up to half its speed away from the creature and become frightened of it until the end of the creature's next turn. This movement doesn't provoke opportunity attacks. While frightened this way, the ratfolk can only take the Dash, Disengage, Dodge, or Hide action. This feature ignores immunity to the frightened condition.
>

> ## Ratfolk Veteran Weapon Operator
>*Medium humanoid (ratfolk), chaotic evil*
> ___

> ***Abandon Post.*** When The ratfolk use Scurry Away it, it may leave a two man weapon it is part of or exit a vehicle without spending any movement and requiring no actions and without provoking attacks of opportunity.
>
> ***Crevice Crawler.*** The ratfolk can move through and stop in a space large enough to fit a creature one size smaller than it without squeezing.
>
> ***Evasion.*** When the ratfolk makes a Dexterity
saving throw to reduce the damage of an effect by half, it
instead takes no damage on a success and only half
damage on a failure
>
> ***Keen Smell.*** The ratfolk has advantage on Wisdom (Perception) checks that rely on smell.
>
> ***Overwhelming Mass x1.*** The first time each turn that the ratfolk hits a creature with an attack, it deals an extra 1 damage per ally it has within 5 feet of its target that isn't incapacitated. The ratfolk can benefit from up to 3 allies this way.
>
> ***Panicked Job.*** The ratfolk may make repair checks on and activate any of the functions of two-creature weapons and siege weapons while frightened by its Scurry Away feature. If it activates any of the functions of a two-creature weapon while frightened this way, the next time the weapon rolls to check for a mishap, it rolls an additional dice.
>
> ### Actions
>
> ***Club.*** *Melee Weapon Attack:* +5 to hit, reach 5 ft., one creature. *Hit:* 5 (1d4 + 3) bludgeoning damage.
>
> ### Reactions
>
> ***Scurry Away.***  When an enemy the ratfolk can see ends its turn, the ratfolk can move up to half its speed away from the creature and become frightened of it until the end of the creature's next turn. This movement doesn't provoke opportunity attacks. While frightened this way, the ratfolk can only take the Dash, Disengage, Dodge, or Hide action. This feature ignores immunity to the frightened condition.
>

> ##### Piloting Vehicles
> If you're using vehicles in your games and want your ratfolk operators to be skilled in piloting them, you can add
> the following attribute to ratfolk weapon operators and ratfolk veteran weapon operators:
>
> ***Panicked Driver.*** The ratfolk can pilot vehicles as an action even while frightened by its Scurry Away feature (this doesn't allow the vehicle to be piloted multiple times in a round). 
>
> Additionally, when the ratfolk uses its Scurry Away feature, it can have a vehicle it's piloting move up to 15 feet away rather than flee on foot.

### Ratfolk Weapons Operator Tactics

Ratfolk weapons operators embody the typical behavior of other ratfolk but are emboldened by their high-powered weaponry. When they have the upper hand, they can be unrelenting bullies, acting recklessly due to their perceived omnipotence, which often leads to their downfall. Conversely, when overpowered or outmatched, panic tends to trigger reckless and drastic decisions, usually resulting in their own demise and potentially that of their foes as well.

Their tactics will vary depending on the weapon they are wielding, but there are some general guidelines:
* When using Scurry Away, ratfolk have the option to either abandon their post by dropping their weapon and fleeing or carry out a panicked job, which involves a hasty attempt at either repairing or firing the weapon again.
* If both ratfolk on the weapons team are wounded and cornered, they will choose to do a panicked job, retreating while desperately attempting to fix or fire the weapon. A frantic weapons team might take whatever risks necessary to maximize the damage potential of their weapon, often to comedic effect.
* If one of the team members has fallen, or if the weapon is damaged (it has less than half its hit points left), the team will likely abandon its post.
* Ratfolk with the optional Panicked Driver trait will abandon their vehicles as soon as they become immobile.

Much of the weaponry and vehicles available to ratfolk present options for high-risk, high-reward tactics. Ratfolk typically take greater risks under two conditions:
* When they are desperate, such as when they are cornered or near death.
* When they have gained the upper hand, they often get overzealous and strive for maximum power, even when it appears unnecessary. 

However, they generally avoid taking risks when the outcome of a fight seems uncertain.

#### Ratfolk Veteran Weapon Operators
Ratfolk veteran weapon operators have survived numerous weapon malfunctions and developed quick reflexes. Their survival is largely due to these reflexes rather than any specific tactical or technical knowledge. This means they generally behave similarly to standard weapon operators.

<br>

### Ratfolk Weapons Operators <br> Art Credit
* Intercessors Arrest - Steve Prescott, Wizards of the Coast

\columnbreak


### Weapon Operator Loot
Because ratfolk are humanoids, most of the valuable goods that can be looted from them are the remains of the equipment they were using or valuables they were carrying or hiding nearby. Most of the challenge of looting ratfolk weapon operators is identifying which materials they're carrying that still have functional value.

Finding valuables can be done using an **Intelligence (Investigation)** or **Wisdom (Perception)** check, depending on the circumstance. Identifying the value of materials the ratfolk was carrying will likely require an **Intelligence (Arcana)** check or a check using proficiency with appropriate tools, such as Smith's Tools, Tinker's Tools, or Alchemist's Supplies.


#### Weapon Operator Loot Tables
The following tables describe the number of items and value of those items the players are able to loot depending on the result of their check or the results of your roll. If they're making checks, you can have them make a separate check for each creature they're looting or use one check for multiple creatures at once to save time.


##### Weapon Operator Loot Table 

| Looting Check Result or 1d20 + 3 |  Loot  |
|:---:|:-----------:|
|  1-5  | 1 5sp Item |
|  6-8 | 1d4(2) 5sp Items | 
|  9-15 | 1d6(3) 5sp Items  |  
|  16-20 | 1d4(2) 1gp Items  |  
|  21+ |  1d6(3) 1gp Items |  

##### Veteran Weapon Operator Loot Table 

| Looting Check Result or 1d20 + 3 |  Loot  |
|:---:|:-----------:|
|  1-5  | 1d6(3) 5sp Items |
|  6-9 | 2d4(5) 5sp Items | 
|  10-16 | 1d6(3) 1gp Items  |  
|  17-21 | 1d6(3) 2gp Items  |  
|  22+ |  2d4(5) 2gp Items |

## Vermin Fiends
These demonic rat beings serve as the avatars of their verminous demon lord. They tower above mortals, their twisted forms a mixture of rat, human, and fiendish features. Their heads are topped with mighty horns, and the flesh peels away from their rat-like skulls, revealing bone etched with demonic sigils. Their long, muscular limbs can wield massive weaponry, yet they are dexterous and nimble with their movements, able to dash across the battle and swiftly dismember foes in the blink of an eye. When not taking action, vermin fiends are intensely twitchy and prone to pacing about with a rat-like restlessness. 

\columnbreak

<br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br>

Mortal ratfolk regard vermin fiends with a mixture of fear and reverence. They only summon these terrifying demons in the most significant of situations, such as when the machinations of their demon lord are in play. Vermin fiends always hold the highest position of authority amongst ratfolk, who show them grudging subservience. As instruments of their demon lord’s will, they serve to guide his mortal pawns and ensure his schemes come to pass.

Vermin fiends come in different variants, and the type of demon to step into the mortal world depends on its summoners and the needs of its verminous demon lord.

### Vermin Fiend Corrupter

These pestilent demons represent the virulent diseases unleashed into the world by their demonic rat lord. They are magical maladies shaped into a fiendish rat form, and where ever they roam, they leave plagues in their wake. They are most often summoned by those ratfolk who revel in disease and spreading sickness, and these vermin fiends consider it their sacred duty to <br> spread their master’s diseases across the mortal realm.

In combat, vermin fiend corrupters unleash a slew of pestilent magics capable of rotting away most foes before they can even reach the demon. Those who attempt to engage it in melee combat will find themselves assaulted by waves of biting parasites whittling away their vitality. The vermin fiend will then summon a pair of sickle blades to quickly dispatch its weakened and rotting enemies in short order.

### Vermin Fiend Deceiver
These devious demons represent their demonic rat lord's cunning and duplicitous nature. They are shadowy fiends whose size and power belies the stealth and subtlety with which they can move and act, always lurking out of sight until an opportunity presents itself. Vermin fiend deceivers are summoned when subtlety and guile are needed rather than conspicuous displays of force, and these cunning fiends manipulate enemy and ally alike to facilitate the schemes of their demon lord. They are most commonly served by assassin clans of ratfolk, and are supreme assassins themselves, able to stalk and slay even the most formidable and well-guarded of targets before disappearing into the shadows.

<br><br>

In combat, vermin fiend deceivers utilize stealth and misdirection to attack from unexpected directions and prevent enemies from surrounding them. They prefer to attack from a distance, utilizing a massive throwing star capable of cutting a swath through armored soldiers before flying back into the demon’s claws. When engaging in melee combat, the vermin fiend utilizes its deadly hexstiletto, a massive dagger the length of a man and capable of piercing through shield and armor alike.

### Vermin Fiend Warbringer

These brutal demons represent their demonic rat lord’s arrogance and ferocity. They are the most common and most warlike of the vermin fiends. Their awe-inspiring presence rallies the normally cowardly ratfolk and drives them into battle with bloody-minded ferocity. Warbringers revel in their effect on others, making dramatic entrances whenever possible and striking majestic poses before their followers. 

In battle, vermin fiend warbringers will often initially lead from the back, driving their minions into the fray. When it comes time for them to join combat, they wield mighty war glaives capable of cleaving through swaths of enemy soldiers. Should the vermin fiend fight a powerful foe, they will utilize a brutal spike-fist capable of inflicting horrendous wounds. These weapons are also useful for delivering underhanded strikes against already overwhelmed enemies. Regardless of the circumstances, when a warbringer slays a foe, it is always sure to do it in the most dramatic and gory way possible, leaving minions struck with awe and foes struck with terror.


<br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br>

### Vermin Fiend Hexseer

These scheming demons represent their demonic rat lord’s plotting and manipulative nature. While all vermin fiends scheme, hexseers carry out plots within plots within plots. All their actions serve to advance the inscrutable and long reaching schemes of their verminous master, and the world’s mortals are simply the tools through which they achieve their ends. They are most often summoned by other so-called “masterminds” among the ratfolk who serve the demonic rat god and require aid in carrying out his schemes.

Hexseers are aided in their plotting by the scryorbs they carry. These large crystal balls enable them to peer into a myriad of different futures and determine how each potential action can further their schemes. 

<br><br>

In dire circumstances, the hexseer can shatter the scryorb, unleashing all its mind-shattering knowledge at once. Creatures caught in its proximity will have their psyches torn apart as they are overwhelmed by the near-infinite possibilities they are suddenly exposed to.

However, these mighty fiends are rarely pushed to use such measures, for they wield arcane power beyond even their other vermin fiend kin. While all vermin fiends can channel magic, hexseers alone are capable of calling down bolts of arching lightning, hurling balls of fire, and unleashing earthquakes capable of leveling settlements. 
___
___

>|18 (+4)|20 (+5)|20 (+5)|22 (+6)|22 (+6)|22 (+6)|

> - **Saving Throws** Con +11, Int +12, Wis +12, Cha +12
> - **Skills** Arcana +12, Deception +18, History +12 Insight +18, Perception +12, Religion +12
> - **Damage Immunities** lightning, poison, psychic
> - **Condition Immunities** blinded, poisoned
> - **Senses** blindsight 60 ft., darkvision 300 ft., truesight 120 ft., passive Perception 22
> - **Languages**  all, telepathy 300 ft.
> - **Challenge** 19 (20,000 XP)   &emsp;&emsp;&emsp; **Proficiency Bonus** +6        
> ___
> ***Crevice Crawler.***  The vermin fiend can move through and stop in a space large enough to fit a creature one size smaller than it without squeezing.
>
> ***Keen Hearing and Smell.*** The vermin fiend has advantage on Wisdom (Perception) checks that rely on hearing or smell.
>
> ***Scry-orb.*** The vermin fiend can perform a 1-hour ceremony to create a scry-orb from nothingness. This ceremony can be performed during a short or long rest, and any previous scry-orb is destroyed if it still exists. The scry-orb vanishes when the vermin fiend dies. The scry-orb is a magic item, and while the vermin fiend holds it, it is under the effects of the *foresight* spell. The scry-orb can be attacked while the vermin fiend is holding it. It has AC 16 and 90 hit points and is immune to poison and psychic damage. Attacks against it have disadvantage if they are made from more than 5 feet away.
>
> ***Overwhelming Mass (6).*** The first time each turn that the vermin fiend hits a creature with an attack, it deals an extra 6 damage per ally it has within 5 feet of its target that isn't incapacitated. The vermin fiend can benefit from up to 3 allies this way.
>
> ***Hexstorm.*** Whenever the vermin fiend calls down lightning with the *call lighting* spell, it first creates another storm cloud centered on a point it can see within 60 feet of it. It then calls down a bolt of lightning from each cloud it has created. A creature can only be damaged by a single bolt at a time. All clouds disappear when the spell ends.
>
>
> ### Actions
> ***Multiattack.*** The vermin fiend makes three attacks.
>
> ***Doom Glaive.*** *Melee Weapon Attack:* +11 to hit, reach 15 ft., one target. *Hit:* 25 (3d12 + 5) slashing damage. 
>
> ***Prehensile Tail.*** *Melee Weapon Attack:* +11 to hit, reach 25 ft., one target. *Hit:* 15 (3d6 + 5) slashing damage. If the target is Large or smaller, the verminlord may push or pull it up to 15 feet away from or towards itself.
>
> ***Shatter Scry-orb.*** The vermin fiend throws its scry-orb at a point within 90 feet of it, causing it to shatter and unleash horrifying visions. Each creature within 30 feet of that point must make a DC 20 Wisdom saving throw, taking 55 (10d10) psychic damage and becoming blinded on a failed save, or half as much damage and not being blinded on a successful one. A creature blinded this way repeats the saving throw at the end of each of its turns, ending the effect on itself on a success.
>
> ***Summon Rat Tide.*** Up to 3 **rat tides** (stat block at end of document) appear in unoccupied spaces within 30 feet of the vermin fiend and remain until destroyed. The rat tides have their own turns but use the vermin fiend's initiative and take their turns immediately after the vermin fiend. The vermin fiend can have up to 3 rat tides summoned by this ability at a time.
>
>
> ***Spellcasting.*** The vermin fiend casts one of the following spells, requiring no components and using Intelligence as its spellcasting ability (spell save DC 20):
>
> At will: *call lightning (5th level)*, *fireball*, *dispel magic (8th level)* *<br>
> 3/day each: *counterspell*, *stinking cloud*, *clairvoyance*, <br>
> 1/day each: *earthquake*, *scrying* (requires its scry-orb)
>
> ### Bonus Actions
> ***Master of Lightning.*** The vermin fiend casts *call lightning* or calls down lighting from a *call lightning* spell it is currently concentrating on. <br>

|  4  |  A clan of ratfolk assassins, led by a **vermin fiend deceiver**, are carrying out a series of sabotages and assassinations designed to spark a war between several city-states. |
