# Example Ratfolk Encounters

## The Vermin Tide <br> (Player Levels: 2-3 or 6-8)
In this encounter, the players wander into the abandoned remains of a ruined town before swarms of rats and ratfolk begin emerging from the shadows to attempt to overrun them. There are two versions of this encounter; one for players in the level 2-3 range and one for players in the level 6-8 range.


### Encounter Context
This encounter doesn't need much setup and only assumes the players are wandering into the ruins of a town they haven't been to recently. Players with experience fighting rats or ratfolk will have better odds with the fight, but it isn't necessary. The players can enter the map from either area 7 or 8.

### Lead Up

The players wander into the remains of a dilapidated town that appears to have been recently abandoned. As they approach the town's market square, they spot dead guardsmen near a well. As they start to investigate the bodies or the area, the ratfolk attack.

### The Ratfolk Mobs
When the encounter begins, a group of random ratfolk will scurry out from a random location on the map. You can roll a Dexterity (Stealth) check against the players' Passive Perception (PP) to determine if the players are surprised or not. To determine what types of ratfolk appear, roll on the Ratfolk Mob table below. To determine where they appear, roll a d8 and match the result with the corresponding map location.

After this first ratfolk mob appears, roll on the Ratfolk Mobs table to determine the type of mob that will appear next, and then roll for the location where that mob will appear. This next mob appears 3 rounds later. Players within 30 feet of that location with a PP of 12 or greater can hear them coming the round before they appear. Players with a PP of 15 or higher can hear them from 60 feet away, and players with a PP of 18 or greater can hear them from anywhere on the map.

Repeat this process until 3 randomly generated ratfolk mobs have appeared. The final mob you roll for will accompany a second "boss mob" as the capstone to the fight, which enters from a different random location. For the level 2-3 version of the encounter, this will be a **ratfolk war vermin** who is the ratfolk leader. For the level 6-8 version of the encounter, it will be a **ratfolk chieftain**, who is the ratfolk leader, accompanied by 2 **ratfolk war vermin**. If the ratfolk leader is slain, all remaining ratfolk will lose their resolve and flee the battle.





\columnbreak

##### Encounter Map: Ruined Town

<br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br>




### Map Description
* **Lighting.** The full moon casts the village in dim light. The building interiors are obscured in darkness.
* **Market Well.** The well in the market center is 30 feet deep. Attempting to climb out requires a DC 10 Strength (Athletics) check. If a ratfolk falls down the well, remove it from combat unless it’s the chieftain or war vermin who show up in the last wave of the encounter. If it is one of these “boss” ratfolk, have it try to climb out of the well (no check required, though it still climbs at half its move speed).
* **Elevated Areas.**  The areas of the map highlighted in green are at a higher elevation than the ground floor of the market. The height difference is described in the map.
* **Cover Areas.** The areas of the map highlighted in yellow are locations the ratfolk may try to retreat to after using their Scurry Away feature. The tents provide half cover to creatures within them and are destroyed after taking 10 damage. A creature can make a DC 11 Strength check to knock a tent over. If a creature is inside a tent that’s been knocked over, it is blinded and moves at half speed until it leaves the tent or cuts its way out with an attack that deals piercing or slashing damage.


<img src='https://i.ibb.co/gdjq8p3/Virmen-Tide-Guide.jpg' style='position:absolute; top:125px; right:2px; width:415px; ' />


\pagebreakNum

<br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br>

##### Ratfolk Mob Table
| 1d4  | Level 2-3 | Level 6-8 | 
|:---:|:-----------:|:-----------:|
|  1 |  3 Ratfolk Warriors |  8 Ratfolk Warriors  |
|  2 | 5 Ratfolk Slaves |  4 Ratfolk War Vermin  | 
|  3 | 1 Ratfolk Warrior & 3 Ratfolk Slaves |  2 Ratfolk War Vermin & 6 Ratfolk Slaves  | 
|  4 | 2 Ratfolk Warriors & 1 Rat Swarm |  2 Groups of 8 Ratfolk Slaves, each appearing at a different location  |

### Encounter Tactics
The ratfolk fight using the same tactics outlined Ratfolk Encounter Guide. Ratfolk are likely to use their Scurry Away feature if they are fighting from a disadvantageous position, there is somewhere nearby they can hide, and there are nearby allies that make it difficult for them to be followed. If a ratfolk mob is near defeat but a new mob will be showing up soon, they are likely to use Scurry Away to attempt to survive long enough for reinforcements to arrive. However, they will not flee from the fight entirely until the ratfolk leader is killed or flees.

#### The Ratfolk Leader
The ratfolk leader, whether it be a war vermin or a chieftain, will use its minions as disposable cannon fodder to be thrown at the players and pin them down. It will then move in and attack anyone that looks weakened or overwhelmed. The leader is recklessly confident and is unlikely to flee unless it is reduced to a quarter of its health or less, or the majority of its minions are dead or near death, and the players still look like they're going strong.

<br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br>

### Aftermath
If all the ratfolk are slain or flee, the players will no longer be in any immediate danger. If the leader escapes, it will likely try to rally a new force of ratfolk and exact its revenge against the players. Though this could take days or even weeks. Any remaining ratfolk in the town will likely flee the players on sight unless they appear vulnerable. If the players were forced to flee, the ratfolk will hound them until they have made it well outside the outskirts of the town.





#### Loot
If the players search the area for valuables, they'll find a chest full of coins the ratfolk were hoarding and a valuable items carried by the ratfolk. They can also loot the individual ratfolk they slew using the guidelines from the Ratfolk Loot Guide. The amount of treasure they find will depend on the level of the encounter.

##### Level 2-3 Encounter Loot
* **Chest:** 1,230 cp, 1,175 sp, 93 gp
* **Individual Ratfolk Minions:** 3 Potions of Healing
* **Ratfolk War Vermin:** Hex Gem worth 100gp
##### Level 6-8 Encounter Loot
* **Chest:** 6,032 cp,7,879 sp, 1,862 gp, 1,132 pp
* **Individual Ratfolk Minions:** 3 Potions of Greater Healing
* **Ratfolk Chieftain:** 1 Fractured Hex Jewel worth 500gp


> ##### Looting Potions During Combat
> You can give the players the opportunity to loot the healing potions from the ratfolk mobs during the battle. Each mob should have a potion carried by one of its ratfolk that the players can grab and use to heal themselves during the fight. This can allow the players to reduce the fight's difficulty if they are willing to expend part of their loot right away.

<img src='https://i.ibb.co/k0Kp3cT/nezumi-cutthroat.jpg' style='position:absolute;right:0px;top:-20px;width:816px;transform:scaleX(1)' />

<img src='https://www.gmbinder.com/images/WGybwnz.png' style='position:absolute; top:50px; right:0px; width:900px; filter:  grayscale(00%) brightness(97%)' />



\pagebreak

#### XP Award: 1,000xp (Level 2-3) or 7,000xp (Level 6-8)
The degree of success the players have in defeating the ratfolk can affect their XP reward. You can use the following potential outcomes as guidelines to modify how much XP you award your players.

* **150% XP:** The majority of the ratfolk and their leader were slain
* **100% XP:** The player won the fight, but the leader or a larger number of ratfolk escaped
* **50% XP:** The players slew the majority of the ratfolk mobs, but retreated before being able to defeat the leader
* **10% XP:** The players were forced to retreat before defeating the majority of the ratfolk mobs


### Adjusting the Difficulty
The encounter assumes you are playing with 4 players in the suggested level range. If the players' levels are outside the suggested level range, or you have a different group size, you can adjust the encounter's difficulty accordingly.

**Easier Encounter.** Remove the second mob that accompanies the ratfolk leader's mob. Cut the XP award by roughly 20%.

**Harder Encounter.** Have a new mob appear each round after the ratfolk leader appears. These new mobs should contain roughly half the number of ratfolk as what's presented in the table. Boost the XP award by roughly 20%.

\columnbreak

### Adventure Follow Ups
If you wish to connect this encounter to a larger adventure, the following hooks can help provide some inspiration:

| d4  | Adventure Hook |
|:---:|:-----------:|
|  1  | After the players secure the town, they learn the remaining ratfolk are moving on to the next village, where a grand festival is taking place. |
|  2  | It turns out the inhabitants of the town did something to anger their god, who sent the ratfolk as divine punishment. Until the god is appeased, swarms of ratfolk continue to infest the town and hunt the surviving inhabitants. |
|  3  | The players learn this was not the only town to fall victim to ratfolk, and a warlord is rallying ratfolk from across the land into a verminous legion. |
|  4  | The players learn of a mysterious noble going from town to town, giving away wealth to the needy. Those who accept his wealth transformed into wicked ratfolk that overrun their town.|

<br>

## The Ruinous Ritual <br> (Player Levels: 16-18)
In this encounter, the players face off against a ratfolk grey prophet performing a dark ritual to gain untold eldritch power. The seer is guarded by multiple ratfolk and protected by an arcane force shield that can only be dispelled by disabling three eldritch generators located across the map.


### Encounter Context
The encounter assumes the players are aware of the ratfolk grey prophet and the ritual he is performing in his underground lair. This encounter’s chamber may even serve as the final room of a dungeon where the players have been fighting their way through ratfolk to reach the grey prophet. 

### Lead Up
When the players arrive at the chamber, they will immediately see the grey prophet performing his dark ritual, surrounded by a magical force shield. The eldritch generators glow as their vile machinery whirls, and the players will see the energy they generate being siphoned to the grey prophet and his shield. You should make it clear to the players that the shield cannot be destroyed or dispelled through conventional means as it is being continually rejuvenated by the generators. Once the grey prophet and his ratfolk minions notice the players, they will immediately attack.

### Map Description
* **Lighting.** The green glow of the ritual and the eldritch engines illuminates the chamber with dim light. If the ritual ends, there will be no light source in the room.
* **Elevated Areas.**  The areas of the map highlighted in green are at a higher elevation than the ground floor of the chamber’s entrance. The height difference is described in the map.
* **Generators.** The generators are Large objects with 30 hit points, AC 18, immunity to psychic and poison damage, and resistance to all spell damage. Attacks against it made from 5 feet away have advantage. A creature within 5 feet of it can make a DC 18 Intelligence (Arcana) check or an Intelligence check using tinker’s tools to disable a generator rather than destroy it.
* **Water.** The water in the champer is 10 feet deep and heavily polluted. Any creature that ends its turn in the water takes 3d6 poison damage.
* **Pipes.** The pipes crisscrossing the chamber have an AC 16 and immunity to psychic and poison damage. If 16 points of damage is dealt to a single section, it ruptures, filling a 10 foot area around it with the effects of the *cloudkill* spell for 1 minute (save DC 16). Once a section of pipe is burst this way, no pipes within 30 feet of it will produce this gas if they are destroyed.



\columnbreak

##### Encounter Map: Ruinous Ritual Chamber

<br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br>

##### Map Legend
* **C:** Ratfolk Council Guard 
* **G:** Eldritch Generator
* **P:** Ratfolk Toxic Wind Bombardier 
* **S:** Ratfolk Grey Prophet
* **V:** Ratfolk War Vermin

### Encounter Tactics
The goal of all the ratfolk in this fight is to kill or drive off the players while protecting the grey prophet’s ability to continue the ritual. Different ratfolk go about this in different ways, but they all answer to the grey prophet.

#### Ratfolk Grey Prophet
The grey prophet can’t move from his location while performing the ritual, but he can still direct the other ratfolk, cast spells, and use his other abilities. The grey prophet is intelligent enough that he can assess what types of saving throws each player will have a more difficult time dealing with, and will play on each player’s weaknesses whenever possible. 

##### Grey Prophet Tactic Tips
* Have him use *chain lightning* as soon as he can target three or more players with it.
* Have him use *fireball* if he can hit two or more players with it. He will deem hitting minions with a fireball acceptable so long as he’s hitting more players than minions and the players have low odds of passing Dexterity saving throws.

<img src='https://i.ibb.co/4Kp08f0/The-Vermin-Ritual-Guide.png' style='position:absolute; top:70px; right:2px; width:415px; ' />


\pagebreakNum


* The *fissure* spell should be used following the same guidelines as the fireball spell, but only if it can be used without affecting an active generator. Any pipes in the fissure’s area are ruptured, and you can have the toxic water flow into the newly formed crevice if it makes sense.
* If the players are spread out, his Lightning Strike attack is usually his best option. Prioritize players surrounded by ratfolk to make use of the extra Overwhelming Mass damage.
* If a player reaches an active generator, that’s a good time to summon a rat tide to hinder that player.
* *Control winds* can be used to hinder player movement and keep them separated, so it’s harder for them to aid isolated and overwhelmed party members.

#### Council Guard and War Vermin
The grey prophet will squeak orders at the council guard in Undercommon throughout the fight. Two council guards are stationed at each generator. If the players split up, sending high-speed characters to quickly disable the generators, the grey prophet will order the council guard to leave their post and charge any fragile players that have been left exposed. This will be done in an attempt to force the other players to pull back to help their allies. If the players take a slower, more methodical approach, the council guard will hold their ground and wait for the players to come to them.
War vermin are more flexible in who and how they’ll fight and <br> will generally help gang up on any player engaged in <br> combat to help add to the damage of Overwhelming <br> Mass.

#### Toxic Wind Bombardiers
Bombardiers will keep their distance and attempt to whittle down players from afar, even if it means hitting a ratfolk or two in the process. They will only engage in melee with players who are fragile and poor hand-to-hand combatants.

#### The Generators are Destroyed
If all the generators are destroyed, the grey prophet will attempt to maintain his position by calling his remaining guards to protect him while he continues to bombard players from afar. If his platform ceases to be safe, or it’s clear he can’t defend it, he will break and flee. Spells like *control winds* and *fissure* can help hinder the players’ pursuit. Any remaining council guard will fight to the death to buy the grey prophet time to escape, but the rest of the ratfolk will break and begin fleeing once they see their leader making a run for it.


### Aftermath
If the players are forced to flee, the ratfolk won’t pursue them out of sight of the chamber. The grey prophet will continue his ritual, and it’s up to you how long it will take him to complete it and what the consequences are. The ritual might be minutes away from completion or hours. The completion of the ritual could result in a variety of deadly consequences, including, but not limited to:
* The grey prophet summons a vermin fiend
* The grey prophet gains the stats of a vermin fiend hexseer
* The grey prophet summons an army of ratfolk
* The grey prophet unleashes terrible disasters, such as plagues, earthquakes, or meteor showers

<br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br>

If the players stop the ritual by destroying the eldritch generators but are forced to flee afterward, the grey prophet will have them repaired and attempt to restart the ritual. This will likely take at least a day, if not more, and the grey prophet may add extra safeguards, such as more minions, in case the players make a second attempt at stopping the ritual.
If the grey prophet is forced to flee, he will likely be foiled in his attempt to complete his ritual and begin plotting revenge against the players.

#### Loot
The players can salvage valuable arcane components from each of the generators. Each generator yields 2d6 x 1,000 gp worth of salvageable goods. If a character with proficiency in Arcana or tinker’s tools salvages a generator, they loot 3d6 x 1000 gp worth of salvageable goods instead. 

The grey prophet wears an eldritch amulet which served as the focal point for the ritual and is worth 10,000 gp.

As this was likely a climatic final battle part of a larger adventure, it is an opportune time to drop in any magic items appropriate to the players’ level that fit the environment or are useful to one or more of the players.

The players can also loot the individual ratfolk they slew using the guidelines from the Ratfolk Loot Guide. 


<img src='https://i.ibb.co/yQKYtjn/nezumi-graverobber-nighteyes-the-desecrator.png' style='position:absolute;right:-90px;top:-10px;width:1000px;transform:scaleX(-1)' />

 <img src='https://www.gmbinder.com/images/cPPYV7h.png' 
  style='position:absolute;right:80px;top:-250px;height:1400px;width:1416px;transform:rotate(280deg)' />

 <img src='https://www.gmbinder.com/images/cPPYV7h.png' 
  style='position:absolute;right:0px;top:140px;height:1400px;width:1416px;transform:rotate(180deg)' />


\pagebreak


#### XP Award: 40,000xp 
The degree of success the players have in defeating the ratfolk can affect their XP reward. You can use the following potential outcomes as guidelines to modify how much XP you award your players.

* **150% XP:** The ritual was stopped and the grey prophet slain
* **100% XP:** The ritual was stopped, but the grey prophet escaped
* **50% XP:** The players destroyed all the generators, thereby delaying the ritual, but fled before defeating the grey prophet
* **10% XP:** The players retreated and failed to stop the ritual



### Adjusting the Difficulty
The encounter assumes you are playing with 4 players in the suggested level range. If the players' levels are outside the suggested level range, or you have a different group size, you can adjust the encounter's difficulty accordingly.

**Easier Encounter.** Reduce the pairs of council guards to solo council guards. Change the XP Award to 33,000 XP.

**Harder Encounter.** Increase the pairs of council guards to trios of council guards. Increase the XP award to 50,000 XP.

\columnbreak

### Adventure Follow Ups
If you wish to connect this encounter to a larger adventure, the following hooks can help provide some inspiration:

| d4  | Adventure Hook |
|:---:|:-----------:|
|  1  | The grey prophet’s ritual is being done at the behest of a demonic master who wishes to tear its way into the mortal realm. |
|  2  | The grey prophet’s ritual transforms the surface world's people into ratfolk to join his ever-growing army of doom. |
|  3  | The grey prophet seeks to complete a ritual to begin a 13-day countdown, heralding the end of the world before his dark god arrives to claim the souls of all its inhabitants. |
|  4  | The grey prophet holds the city above his lair hostage and threatens to unleash a magical calamity if they do not meet his demands.|

<br>
